Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate
7 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Combining Goods of Different Types in Mudarabah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on combining mudarabah goods of different types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on combining goods of different types in mudarabah, and identify the practical consequence of the difference.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa treats different types separately due to hidden disparity; Sahibayn allow combination by judge or consent.

In mudarabah, the classification of goods (a'yan) into same or different types affects how profit is calculated. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement: Abu Hanifa insists on strict separation, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow combination under certain conditions. This lesson unpacks that ikhtilaf and its practical impact.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Default Rule
The default Hanafi rule is that goods of different types (ajnas) are treated separately for profit calculation. This means each type's value is compared to the capital allocated to it.
2
Abu Hanifa's Position
Abu Hanifa holds that different types are always separate due to great disparity in hidden meanings (ma'ani batina). No combination is allowed.
E.g., a male slave and a horse are different types.
3
Sahibayn's Position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad agree in principle but allow combination if the judge sees overall benefit (salah) or if the parties mutually agree. Then they are combined as one type.
Combination changes profit calculation: all goods pooled, profit appears when total value exceeds total capital.
4
Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
If combined, profit may be realized sooner or later depending on individual item fluctuations. It also affects the mudarib's ownership share and distribution.
Example: one item gains, another loses; combined may show profit, separate may not.
5
Relied-Upon Position
The default (Abu Hanifa) is the mufta bihi unless circumstances justify combination. The text cites al-Kifayah and does not give explicit tarjih.
Later Hanafi works may clarify.

Source Text

[١] قوله : أعياناً ؛ أي أجناساً مختلفة حقيقة أو حكماً، حتى لو كان أعياناً من جنس واحد كل عين يساوي رأس المال، يظهر الربح كما إذا اشترى فرسين كلُّ واحدٍ منها يساوي ألفاً، ورأس المال ألف كان له ربعُها ، حتى لو وهب رجلٌ وسلّمه إليه صح. لا يظهر الربح، بل كلُّ واحدٍ يصلح أن يكون رأس المال ؛ لأنه يمكن أن يهلَكَ ما سواه، ويبقى واحد فقط، فلا رجحان لأحد لكونه رأس المال، أو ربحاً. ثُمَّ إذا زادت القيمة بعد الدعوة حتى صارَ قيمة الولد ألفاً وخمسمئة ظَهَرَ الربح ، فنفذت الدعوة السابقة، ويثبت النسب ، وعتق الولد لقيام ملكه في البعض أما العبد فعند أبي حنيفة له أجناس مختلفة ؛ لفحش التفاوت في المعاني الباطنة، وعندهما كذلك ، إلا أن يرى القاضي الصلاح في الجميع، أو يتراضوا على ذلك ، فحينئذ يجمع. كذا في «الكفاية». [١] قوله : لا يظهر الربح ؛ فإذا لم يظهر الربح لم يكن للمضارب في الجارية ملك، وبدون الملك لا يثبت الاستيلاء. [٢] قوله : ثم إذا زادت القيمة...الخ ؛ ولو لم تزد قيمة الولد على ألف، وزادت قيمة الأم حتى صارت ألفاً وخمسمئة صارتِ الجارية أم ولد للمضارب، ويضمن لرب المال ألف درهم ومئتين وخمسين درهماً ؛ لأنها لما زادت قيمتها ظهر فيها الربح ، وملك المضارب بعض الربح ، فنفذت دعوته فيها. ويجب عليه لرب المال رأس ماله، وهو ألف، ويجب عليه أيضاً نصيبه من الربح ، مائتان وخمسون درهماً ، فإذا وصل إلى يده ألف استوفى رأس المال، وصار الولد وهو كله ربحاً، فيملك المضارب منه نصفه فيعتق عليه، وما لم يصل إلى ربِّ المال الألف فالولد رقيق، ثم يأخذ منه مئتين وخمسين على أنه نصيبه من الربح. ولو ازدادت قيمتها عتق الولد، وصارت الجارية أمّ ولد له ؛ لأن الربح ظهر في كل واحد منها، ويأخذ رأس المال من المضارب وما بقي من نصيبه من الربح، ويضمن أيضاً نصف عقرها ؛ لأنه لما استوفى رأس المال ظهر أنه ربح ؛ لأنَّ عقر مال المضاربة يكون للمضاربة، ويسعى الغلامُ في نصيب ربِّ المال، ويسقط عنه نصيب المضارب. ذكره العيني، وغيره.
[1] His saying: 'goods (a'yan)' means different types in reality or legally. Even if the goods are of one type, each item equal to the capital, profit appears, as if he buys two horses each worth one thousand, and the capital is one thousand, he has one-fourth of them. Even if a man gives (one) as a gift and hands it over to him, it is valid. Profit does not appear; rather, each one is suitable to be the capital because it is possible that the other perishes and only one remains, so there is no preference for either as capital or profit. Then if the value increases after the claim until the child's value becomes one thousand five hundred, profit appears, the previous claim is executed, lineage is established, and the child is emancipated due to his ownership in part. As for the slave (male), according to Abu Hanifa, he has different types due to the great disparity in hidden meanings, and according to both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) as well, unless the judge sees benefit in all, or they mutually agree, then they are combined. Thus in al-Kifayah. [1] His saying: 'Profit does not appear' – if profit does not appear, the mudarib has no ownership in the slave-girl, and without ownership, istila' (possession) is not established. [2] His saying: 'Then if the value increases...' – even if the child's value does not increase beyond one thousand, and the mother's value increases to one thousand five hundred, the slave-girl becomes umm walad for the mudarib, and he guarantees to the principal one thousand dirhams and two hundred fifty dirhams, because when her value increased, profit appeared in her, and the mudarib owned some profit, so his claim in her is executed. He owes the principal his capital, which is one thousand, and also his share of profit, two hundred fifty dirhams. So if one thousand reaches his hand, he has satisfied the capital, and the child becomes all profit, so the mudarib owns half of it and it is emancipated for him. As long as the one thousand has not reached the principal, the child remains a slave. Then he takes from him two hundred fifty as his share of profit. If her value increases further, the child is emancipated and the slave-girl becomes umm walad for him, because profit appears in each of them. He takes the capital from the mudarib and the remainder of his share of profit, and also guarantees half of her 'uqr (dower) because when he satisfied the capital, it becomes apparent that it is profit; because the 'uqr of mudarabah property belongs to the mudarabah. The boy seeks compensation for the principal's share, and the mudarib's share is dropped. Mentioned by al-'Ayni and others.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling regarding a mudarib's claim of paternity and the role of profit. It begins by glossing the term 'a'yan' (specific goods) from the matn. The commentator explains that if the mudarabah capital is converted into goods that are all of different types (in reality or legally), profit is determined by comparing each item to the capital. If the goods are of one type, each item equal to the capital, profit is not immediately apparent because any one item could represent the capital if the others perish. For example, if the mudarib buys two horses each worth 1000 dirhams with a capital of 1000, he owns one-fourth of each (since the capital is half of the total value, but the mudarib's share of profit is half of the remaining after capital, so effectively one-fourth). If the mudarib gifts one horse, it is valid. However, profit is not realized until the total value exceeds the capital. The condition for the mudarib's claim of paternity to be effective is that profit must have appeared, giving him ownership in the slave-girl. If the child's value increases after the claim (e.g., to 1500), profit appears, the earlier claim is executed, lineage is established, and the child is emancipated proportionally to the mudarib's share. The passage then notes an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the classification of goods: according to Abu Hanifa, if the goods are of different types (e.g., a male slave), they are considered different due to significant disparity in hidden attributes, so the same rule applies. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), the same applies unless the judge sees overall benefit or the parties agree, in which case they can be combined (i.e., treated as one type). The commentary then provides further detail: if the child's value does not increase but the mother's value does (to 1500), the mother becomes umm walad for the mudarib. He must pay the principal 1250 dirhams (1000 capital + 250 profit share). Once the capital is paid, the child becomes entirely profit, half owned by the mudarib and freed, while the other half remains the principal's until paid. If values increase further, both child and mother are affected: the child is freed, the mother is umm walad, and the mudarib must pay the capital and his remaining profit share, plus half of the 'uqr (compensation for using the slave-girl) because after capital satisfaction, it is profit. The slave-boy then works to compensate the principal's share, and the mudarib's share is dropped. This is based on the principle that the 'uqr of mudarabah property belongs to the mudarabah itself. The commentator attributes this to al-'Ayni and others.

Key Terms
أعيان (a'yan): Specific, tangible goods purchased with mudarabah capital, as opposed to cash.
عقر (uqr): Compensation for using a slave-girl, typically paid to the owner for loss of value due to pregnancy or childbirth.
استيلاء (istila'): Legal possession or control, which is a prerequisite for a valid claim of paternity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, under what condition do the Sahibayn allow combining goods of different types in mudarabah?
A) Always, as a general rule.
B) Only if the goods are of the same value.
C) If the judge sees benefit or the parties mutually agree.
D) Never; they follow Abu Hanifa strictly.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa treats different-type goods separately; Sahibayn allow combination by judge or consent.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
advanced
12 min
Mudarib's Paternity Claim and Profit Realization
Expands rulings on paternity claim by mudarib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for a mudarib's paternity claim in a mudarabah slave-girl, explain the effect of profit realization on ownership, and calculate the compensation due to the capital owner.

Core Idea
A mudarib's paternity claim is valid only when profit appears—asset value exceeds capital.

This lesson expands a key ruling in Mudarabah: a mudarib's claim of paternity to a child born of a slave-girl from the partnership capital. The ruling hinges on profit realization—the mudarib must own part of the slave-girl, which occurs only when her value (or that of her child) exceeds the initial capital. The commentator, drawing from al-Kifayah and al-Kafi, explains the legal consequences: the child becomes free, the mother becomes umm walad, and the mudarib must compensate the capital owner for his share of the mother's value. We will walk through the conditions, the reasoning by analogy, and the practical compensation calculations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
The act is the mudarib claiming paternity of a child born to a slave-girl from the mudarabah capital. The condition for validity is that profit must appear—the value of the slave-girl or child must exceed the capital so that the mudarib owns part of the profit and thus part of the slave-girl.
Without profit appearance, the mudarib has no ownership and the claim is ineffective.
2
Trace the key legal principle
The principle is that paternity is established by ownership of the mother. Since the mudarib does not own the capital outright, he only acquires partial ownership when profit appears. The text derives this from the general rule that a slave's child follows the mother's owner.
Ownership here is not full but partial, contingent on profit share.
3
Follow the reasoning (talil) via analogy
The text compares the mudarib's guarantee of half the mother's value to a man who marries his brother's slave-girl, then inherits her upon the brother's death. In both cases, ownership is acquired without a deliberate freeing act, yet compensation is due to co-owners. This analogy (qiyas) justifies the mudarib's compensation.
The guarantee is of ownership, not of injury, so no wrongful act is required.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
Regarding the slave (the child), Abu Hanifa holds that different types of property (e.g., mother and child) are considered separately due to gross disparity in hidden qualities. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) also generally require separation but allow a judge to combine if beneficial or if parties agree.
This affects how profit is calculated across multiple assets.
5
Apply compensation rules to scenarios
The lesson details several scenarios based on which asset increases in value. The mudarib compensates the capital owner for half the mother's value (the capital owner's share) when the capital is recovered, but not for the freeing itself. Compensation is for the acquisition of the capital owner's share through ownership.
The freeing is automatic due to ownership, not a deliberate act, so no compensation for freesing.

[3] His statement: 'so the slave-girl is all profit'; and the reason why the slave-girl was not made capital and all the child profit is because what is due upon the child is of the same type as the capital, and it is given priority in recovery, so its designation for capital is more appropriate, and when the slave-girl became profit, her dower due upon the mudarib also becomes profit, so it is between them. Thus in al-Kifayah. [4] His statement: 'so he guarantees half of its value'; which is the share of the capital owner, and this is like if a man marries the slave-girl of his brother, then the brother, the master, dies, leaving that slave-girl as inheritance between that husband and another brother; the husband owns her without any action, so he guarantees the share of his partner, that is the other brother. [0] His statement: 'so action is not a condition for it'; because the guarantee of ownership returns to the subject, so it is equal regarding transgression and otherwise, like a sleeping person if he rolls onto something and destroys it, then it becomes apparent that the guarantee of ownership does not require action, rather it depends on ownership, which is present then. Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage from the book of Mudarabah is an expansion (sharh) on the rulings regarding a mudarib's claim of paternity in a slave-girl that is part of the mudarabah capital. The core issue is how profit is realized and how it affects the validity of the claim and the ownership status of the mother and child. The commentator explains that initially, if the assets have not increased in value, profit does not appear, and thus the mudarib has no ownership in the slave-girl to support his claim. However, if after the claim the value of the child (or the mother) increases such that the total exceeds the capital, profit becomes apparent, and the claim is executed: the child is free (since the mudarib owns part of the profit and thus part of the child), and the mother becomes an umm walad (a slave concubine who begets a child to her master), which entitles her to freedom upon the master's death. The passage then details various scenarios depending on which asset increases in value. There is an intra-Hanafi mention: regarding the slave (the child), Abu Hanifa holds that different types [of property?] are considered separately due to gross disparity in hidden qualities, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) agree but allow the judge to combine if beneficial or if the parties agree. The commentary emphasizes that the mudarib does not owe compensation to the capital owner for the freeing because the freeing is a legal consequence of ownership, not a direct action by the mudarib. However, if the capital owner recovers his capital, the mudarib must compensate him for half the value of the mother (the capital owner's share) because the mother becomes all profit and the mudarib owns her through the claim, making this a guarantee of ownership that does not require a wrongful act. This is similar to a man inheriting a slave-girl from his brother whom he had married—he owns her without action but must compensate the co-heir.

Key Terms
المضاربة (al-mudarabah): A commercial partnership where one party (rabb al-mal) provides capital and another (mudarib) provides labor, with profits shared according to agreement.
أم ولد (umm walad): A female slave who bears a child to her master, thereby gaining freedom upon the master's death, and the child is free.
ربح (ribh): Profit, the increase in the value of the mudarabah capital over the initial investment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the mudarib's paternity claim in a slave-girl of the mudarabah become effective?
A) Immediately upon making the claim.
B) Only after the capital owner agrees.
C) When the value of the slave-girl or her child exceeds the capital, showing profit.
D) After the mudarib compensates the capital owner.

Key Takeaway
The mudarib's paternity claim in a mudarabah slave-girl is valid only when profit appears (value exceeds capital), and the mudarib compensates the capital owner for his share of the mother's value, not for the freeing itself.

Mudarib's Liability for Slave-Girl Becoming Umm Walad
Explains mudarib's non-liability for slave-girl due to ownership by claim, and obligation to guarantee half value.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between daman i'taq and daman tamalluk to determine a mudarib's liability when a slave-girl purchased with capital becomes an umm walad.

Core Idea
The mudarib is not liable for the slave-girl because emancipation is by claim, not action.

In a mudarabah, the mudarib (partner-manager) purchases a slave-girl with capital, then claims her child, making her an umm walad. Does he owe compensation to the capital owner (rabb al-mal) for the slave-girl? The Hanafi answer is nuanced: he does not guarantee the slave-girl herself because her emancipation is a legal consequence of his claim and deferred ownership, not his direct act. However, he must guarantee half her value after returning the capital, based on the distinction between a guarantee requiring an act (daman i'taq) and a guarantee arising from ownership (daman tamalluk). This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning and analogies used by the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and scenario
Read the passage to understand the specific scenario: mudarib claims paternity of a slave-girl bought with capital, making her umm walad. Note the core ruling: 'He does not guarantee anything to the owner of the capital' for the slave-girl herself.
Focus on the phrase 'لا يضمن لرب المال شيئاً'.
2
Understand the proof: why no act
Examine the text's reasoning: emancipation is by claim and ownership, but ownership is deferred. Therefore, the mudarib has 'no act' in the emancipation. This prevents the liability from being a guarantee of an act (daman i'taq).
The key phrase: 'و لا صنع له فيه' (he has no act in it).
3
Distinguish between daman i'taq and daman tamalluk
The text contrasts two types of guarantee: daman i'taq requires a positive act (like directly freeing a slave), while daman tamalluk does not—it arises from ownership itself. Here, the mudarib's guarantee is of ownership (tamalluk), not act.
Refer to the notes saying 'ضمان إعتاق' vs 'ضمان تملك'.
4
Apply the distinction to options and liability
The mudarib has two options: seek earnings (istis'a) from the slave-girl to repay capital + half profit, or free her and guarantee half her value. After receiving the capital, he must guarantee half value because the slave-girl is profit, and her ownership triggers daman tamalluk.
The text says: 'فله الاستعساء... أو الاعتاق... فيضمن نصف قيمتها'.
5
Examine the analogies to solidify the principle
The commentary gives two analogies: (1) a man inherits a slave-girl from his brother and must compensate co-heir; (2) a sleeping person rolls onto something and destroys it—liable because ownership is established. Both illustrate daman tamalluk without an act.
Focus on the phrases 'كما إذا تزوج رجل جارية أخيه' and 'كالنائم إذا انقلب'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يضمن لرب المال شيئاً ؛ لأنَّ عتقه بالدعوة وبالملك، والملك مؤخَّرٌ فيضاف إليه، ولا صنع له فيه ؛ لأنه ضمان إعتاق، فلا بد له من صنع، فله الاستعساء في رأس المال ونصف الربح أو الاعتاقِ عند أبي حنيفة، فإذا قَبَضَ الألف فله أن يُضَمِّنَ المضارب الذي ادعى الولد نصف قيمة الأم ؛ لأنَّ الألف المأخوذ صارَ رَأسَ المال ؛ لتقدمه استيفاء، فالجارية كلها ربح لكن نَفَذتِ الدعوة السابقة وصارت أم ولد له، فيضمن نصف قيمتها ، لأنه ضمانُ تَمَلكِ فلا يشترط له صنع
[0] قوله : ولا يضمن لرب المال ؛ يعني موسراً كان أو معسراً ؛ لأن نفوذ العتق بمعنى حكمي لا صنع للمضارب فيه، وهو ظهورُ الفضل في قيمته، وذلك يمنع وجوب الضمان عليه لشريكه. كذا في «الكافي».
[1] قوله : فيضاف...الخ ؛ لأنَّ الحكم إذا ثبت بعلةٍ ذات وصفين يضاف إلى آخرهما وجوداً. كما مر آنفاً.
[2] قوله : فالجارية كلّها ربح ؛ وإنما لم يجعل الجارية رأس المال وجميع الولد ربحاً؛ لأن ما يجب على الولد من جنس رأس المال، وإنه مقدم في الاستيفاء، فكان تعينه لرأس المال أولى، ولما صارتِ الجارية ربحاً فعقرها الواجب على المضارب يصير ربحاً أيضاً، فيكون بينهما. كذا في «الكفاية».
[3] قوله : فيضمن نصف قيمتها ؛ وهو نصيب رب المال، وهذا كما إذا تزوج رجل جارية أخيه فمات الأخ المولى، وترك تلك الجارية ميراثاً بين ذلك الزوج وأخ آخر، فالزوج يملكها من غير صنعه، فيضمن نصيب شريكه، وهو الأخ الآخر.
[4] قوله : فلا يشترط له صنع ؛ فإنَّ ضمان التملك يرجع إلى المحلّ، فيستوي فيه للتعدي، وغيره كالنائم إذا انقلب على شيءٍ فأتلفه فظهرَ أنَّ ضمان التملك لا يستدعي صنعاً، بل يعتمد الملك وهو حاصل حينئذ.
He does not guarantee anything to the owner of the capital because his emancipation is by the claim and by ownership, and ownership is deferred, so it is attributed to him, and he has no act in it; because it is a guarantee of emancipation, so there must be an act. So he has the right to seek earnings (istis'a) in the capital and half the profit or emancipation according to Abu Hanifa. When he receives the thousand, he can make the mudarib who claimed the child guarantee half the value of the mother because the thousand received became capital due to its precedence in receipt, so the slave-girl is entirely profit, but the prior claim took effect and she became an umm walad for him, so he guarantees half her value because it is a guarantee of ownership, so an act is not required for it. [0] He said: 'And he does not guarantee to the owner of the capital' meaning whether he is wealthy or poor because the effectiveness of emancipation is in a legal sense, without any act by the mudarib, and it is the appearance of surplus in her value, and that prevents the obligation of guarantee upon him for his partner. As in al-Kafi. [1] He said: 'so it is attributed' etc. because when a ruling is established by a cause having two descriptions, it is attributed to the last one in existence, as previously mentioned. [2] He said: 'so the slave-girl is entirely profit' and it was not made that the slave-girl is capital and all the offspring are profit because what is obligatory upon the offspring is of the same type as the capital, and it has precedence in receipt, so its assignment to capital is more appropriate; and when the slave-girl became profit, her dower (futur) obligatory upon the mudarib also becomes profit, thus it is between them. As in al-Kifaya. [3] He said: 'so he guarantees half her value' which is the share of the owner of the capital, and this is like if a man marries his brother's slave-girl and the brother (the master) dies, leaving that slave-girl as inheritance between that husband and another brother, the husband owns her without any act, so he guarantees the share of his partner, the other brother. [4] He said: 'so an act is not required for it' because guarantee of ownership reverts to the thing itself, so it is equal regarding transgression and otherwise, like a sleeping person who turns over onto something and destroys it, so it appears that guarantee of ownership does not require an act, but rather depends on ownership, which is present then.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (talil) from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah, explaining the scenario where a mudarib (partner in a mudarabah) uses the capital to buy a slave-girl, then claims paternity of her child, making her an umm walad. The key issue is whether the mudarib is liable to the capital owner (rabb al-mal) for the slave-girl's value. The text rules that the mudarib does not guarantee anything to the capital owner regarding the slave-girl herself because her emancipation (by becoming umm walad) occurs through the claim (da'wa) and ownership, but the ownership is deferred (since the slave-girl is part of the capital originally), so the emancipation is attributed to the mudarib's ownership, not his action. However, since the mudarib has no act in this emancipation (it occurs automatically upon claim), the guarantee here is not a guarantee of an act (daman i'taq) which requires the guarantor's action, but rather a guarantee of ownership (daman tamalluk). Therefore, the mudarib has the option to either seek earnings (istis'a) from the slave-girl to pay off the capital and half the profit, or to free her and compensate. When the mudarib later receives the capital (the thousand), the slave-girl becomes pure profit. But the prior claim already made her an umm walad, so the mudarib owns her. He must then guarantee half her value to the capital owner, because the capital owner's share of the profit was half. The commentary analogizes this to a case where a man inherits a slave-girl from his brother and must compensate the co-heir. The underlying principle is that daman tamalluk (guarantee of ownership) does not require a positive act; it arises from the fact of ownership itself, even if obtained without action (e.g., a sleeping person who rolls onto and destroys something is liable because ownership of the thing is established by the act of atlaf, but here ownership of the slave-girl is by claim, not by destruction). The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) is that the mudarib can seek istis'a in the capital and half the profit, or free her directly. This is a Zahir al-Riwayah position. There is no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf mentioned here.

Key Terms
ضمان إعتاق (daman i'taq): Liability for emancipation, i.e., a guarantee that requires a positive act of freeing the slave.
ضمان تملك (daman tamalluk): Liability arising from ownership itself, without requiring a positive act of causing the ownership.
استعساء (istis'a'): Seeking earnings from the slave (by hiring out or using her labor) to pay off a debt or compensate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why does the mudarib not guarantee the slave-girl to the capital owner (rabb al-mal)?
A) Because the mudarib already paid for her from his own money.
B) Because the emancipation is by claim and ownership, and ownership is deferred, so the mudarib has no act in the emancipation.
C) Because the capital owner authorized the purchase.
D) Because the slave-girl is still part of the capital.

Key Takeaway
The mudarib is not liable for the slave-girl to the capital owner because emancipation is by claim and deferred ownership, but he must guarantee half her value because he owns her, and the guarantee is of ownership (daman tamalluk), not of act (daman i'taq).

Mudarib Handing Capital to Another Mudarib: Liability and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains ruling on mudarib giving capital to another and liability for loss

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a mudarib becomes liable for handing capital to another mudarib without permission, and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, Zufar, and Hasan ibn Ziyad.

Core Idea
A mudarib does not guarantee the capital upon mere handover; liability arises only when the second mudarib works with it.

In this passage, we explore a nuanced rule of mudarabah (Islamic partnership) where the mudarib himself becomes the capital provider for another mudarib. The key question is: at what point does the first mudarib become liable to the original owner if the capital is lost? The Hanafi school presents multiple views, and we will identify the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the parties
The act is a mudarib handing over the mudarabah capital to another mudarib without permission from the original owner (rabb al-mal). The parties are: first mudarib (who becomes a rabb al-mal for the second), second mudarib, and the original owner.
This is a 'compound mudarabah' (mudarabah murakkabah).
2
State the Zahir al-Riwayah position
According to the apparent narration from Abu Hanifa, supported by the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): the first mudarib is not liable merely by handing over; liability arises only when the second mudarib works with the capital, regardless of profit or loss.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi variations
Hasan ibn Ziyad narrates that the first mudarib is not liable even with work unless the second makes a profit. Zufar and another narration from Abu Yusuf hold that liability arises upon mere handover, whether the second acts or not.
The latter view is also held by the three other imams (Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad).
4
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: in a Hanafi court, if capital is lost before the second mudarib works, the first is not liable; under Zufar's view, he would be liable immediately.
The tarjih is for the Zahir al-Riwayah position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المضارب الذي يضارب
ولا يَضمَنُ المضاربُ بدفعِهِ مضاربةً
[1] قوله : باب المضارب يضارب ؛ المشهور أنَّ المصنف له لما فرغ عن بيان المضاربة المفردة شرع في بيان المركبة ، فإنَّ المركب يتلو المفرد طبعاً، فكذا وضعاً، لكن فيه كلام ؛ فإنَّ مضاربة المضارب وإن كانت بعد مضاربة ربِّ المال إلا أنها مفردة أيضاً غير مركبة من المضاربتين. فالأولى أن يقال : لما فرغ المصنف له عن بيان حكم المضاربة الأولى شرع في بيانِ حكم المضاربة الثانية، فإنَّ الثانية تتلو الأولى أبداً.
وفي قوله : باب ؛ يصح التنوين وعدمه، أما التنوين فعلى أنه خبر مبتدأ محذوف ؛ أعني هذا، وقوله : المضارب مبتدأ وخبره يضارب فالمعنى : إنَّ المضارب تقعُ منه المضاربة، وأما عدم التنوين فعلى أنه مضاف إلى قوله : المضارب يضارب.
وقوله : يضارب ؛ إمّا صفة لقوله : المضارب أو حال منه، لكن في تقدير الصفة خدشة ظاهرة وهو عدم التطابق بين الموصوف وصفته في التعريف والتنكير؛ لكون الجملة في حكم النكرة، اللّهُمَّ إلا أن يقال : اللام في المضارب للجنس، فيكون بمنزلة النكرة.
وعلى الحالية يراد أنَّ الحال لا تجيء من المضاف إليه إلا في صور ثلاث، وهذا ليس منها ، فالأولى في صورة الإضافة ما في بعض النسخ : باب المضارب الذي يضارب.
[2] قوله : ولا يضمن المضارب...الخ ؛ يعني إنَّ المضارب إذا دفع مال المضاربة إلى غيره مضاربة بلا إذن من ربِّ المال فلا ضمان على المضارب إذا هلك المالُ بمجرَّدِ الدفع ما لم يعمل المضارب الثاني في المال، وإذا عمل ضمن الدافع سواء ربح الثاني أو لا. وهذا في ظاهر الرواية عن الإمام، وهو قولهما، وفي رواية الحسن عن الإمام: إنه لا يضمن بالعمل أيضاً ما لم يربح ، وعند زفر: يضمن بالدفع سواء تصرف أو لم يتصرّف، وهو رواية عن أبي يوسف، هو قول الأئمة الثلاثة.
Chapter of the mudarib who gives a mudarabah [to another]. And the mudarib does not guarantee by his giving a mudarabah. [1] He said: 'Chapter of the mudarib who gives a mudarabah' – the well-known view is that the author, when he finished explaining the single mudarabah, began explaining the compound mudarabah, because the compound naturally follows the single, and thus in arrangement. But there is discussion; because the mudarabah of the mudarib, although it comes after the mudarabah of the owner of capital, is also single, not compounded of two mudarabahs. So it is better to say: when the author finished explaining the ruling of the first mudarabah, he began explaining the ruling of the second mudarabah, for the second always follows the first. And regarding his saying 'chapter', tanwin is permissible and also its omission. As for tanwin, it is as if it is the predicate of an omitted subject, i.e., 'this', and his saying 'the mudarib' is a subject and its predicate 'gives a mudarabah', so the meaning is that the mudarib performs a mudarabah. As for the omission of tanwin, it is as an idafa to his saying 'the mudarib gives a mudarabah'. And his saying 'gives a mudarabah' is either a description of 'the mudarib' or a circumstantial accusative from it, but in considering it a description there is a clear flaw: the lack of agreement between the described and the description in definiteness and indefiniteness, because the sentence is treated as indefinite. However, it could be said that the 'alif lam' in 'al-mudarib' is for the genus, so it is like an indefinite. And on the circumstantial view, it is intended that the circumstantial does not come from the mudaf ilayhi except in three cases, and this is not among them. So the better form in the case of idafa is what is in some copies: 'Chapter of the mudarib who gives a mudarabah'. [2] He said: 'And the mudarib does not guarantee...' meaning that if the mudarib gives the capital of the mudarabah to another as a mudarabah without permission from the owner of the capital, then there is no guarantee upon the mudarib if the capital is lost merely by the handing over, as long as the second mudarib has not worked with the capital. And if he works, then the giver (the first mudarib) guarantees, whether the second profits or not. This is in the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah) from Imam Abu Hanifa, and it is the saying of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And in a narration from Hasan (ibn Ziyad) from Imam: he does not guarantee even with work unless the second profits. And according to Zufar: he guarantees upon the handing over, whether the second acts or not, and it is a narration from Abu Yusuf; it is the saying of the three Imams (i.e., Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad).
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage opens a new chapter on the compound mudarabah (mudarabah of a mudarib). The commentary first explains the chapter heading grammatically and conceptually, noting that the author transitions from single mudarabah to compound mudarabah (where the mudarib himself becomes a rabb al-mal for another mudarib). Then the main ruling is stated: the mudarib (first partner) does not guarantee the capital if he hands it to another mudarib without permission from the original owner, merely by handing over; liability only arises when the second mudarib works (i.e., trades) with the capital. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) in Zahir al-Riwayah. Then it records an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: in a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad, the first mudarib is not liable even with work, unless profit is made. Another view, from Zufar and also narrated from Abu Yusuf, is that the first mudarib is liable upon mere handover, whether the second acts or not. The text adds that this last view (liability upon handover) is the position of the three other imams (Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad). The passage thus presents the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn) as the relied-upon view, with the mufta bihi being that liability attaches upon work by the second mudarib, not mere handover. The commentary emphasizes the Zahir al-Riwayah status of this ruling.

Key Terms
مضارب (mudarib): The person who receives capital in a mudarabah partnership and trades with it; here also the mudarib who becomes a rabb al-mal by handing capital to another.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known and authoritative transmission from the founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) through the six books of Muhammad al-Shaybani.
رب المال (rabb al-mal): The owner of the capital in a mudarabah contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Zahir al-Riwayah (apparent narration) from Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, when does a mudarib become liable for the capital he hands over to another mudarib without permission?
A) Immediately upon handing over the capital.
B) Only when the second mudarib works with the capital.
C) Only if the second mudarib makes a profit.
D) Only if the capital is destroyed by a thief.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi mufta bihi, a mudarib becomes liable for capital handed to another only when that other works with the capital, not upon mere handover.

Liability of a Mudarib Sub-Contracting Mudarabah Without Permission: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explaining liability of mudarib sub-contracting mudarabah without permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three intra-Hanafi positions on when a mudarib becomes liable for sub-contracting mudarabah capital and identify which position is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
A mudarib is not liable for merely handing over capital; liability arises only when the second mudarib works with it.

This passage from Sharh al-Wiqayah examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: when does a mudarib become liable if he sub-contracts the mudarabah capital to another without the capital owner's permission? The base text states no liability upon handing over, but the commentators explore three distinct views within the school. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to identify the operative ruling (mufta bihi) and appreciate how Hanafi scholars weigh evidence within their own tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text ruling
Locate the statement 'ولا يضمن المضارب بدفعه مضاربة' – the mudarib is not liable for handing over. This is the foundation.
The base text is from the matn of al-Wiqayah, commented on here.
2
State the Zahir al-Riwayah position
The manifest transmission (Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn): no liability upon handing over; liability when the second mudarib works. Understand the reasoning: handing over is a permitted deposit; work transforms it into mudarabah.
3
Identify the alternative views
Two other views: (a) Al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa – liability only upon profit; (b) Zufar – liability upon handing over. Note the different triggers: work vs. profit vs. handing over.
4
Examine the proofs for each view
For Zahir al-Riwayah: analogy to deposit (wadi'ah) – no liability without work. For Hasan: after work it is speculation (ibdaa'), partnership only upon profit. For Zufar: handing over without permission is a tort.
The qiyas panel in the toolbox compares to deposit.
5
Apply the tarjih and determine the mufta bihi
The commentator favors the Zahir al-Riwayah view as the relied-upon position. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that the first mudarib compensates only if the second works, regardless of profit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المضارب الذي يضارب
ولا يَضمَنُ المضاربُ بدفعِهِ مضاربةً
[١]
قوله : باب المضارب يضارب ؛ المشهور أنَّ المصنف له لما فرغ عن بيان المضاربة المفردة شرع في بيان المركبة ، فإنَّ المركب يتلو المفرد طبعاً، فكذا وضعاً، لكن فيه كلام ؛ فإنَّ مضاربة المضارب وإن كانت بعد مضاربة ربِّ المال إلا أنها مفردة أيضاً غير مركبة من المضاربتين. فالأولى أن يقال : لما فرغ المصنف له عن بيان حكم المضاربة الأولى شرع في بيانِ حكم المضاربة الثانية، فإنَّ الثانية تتلو الأولى أبداً.
وفي قوله : باب ؛ يصح التنوين وعدمه، أما التنوين فعلى أنه خبر مبتدأ محذوف ؛ أعني هذا، وقوله : المضارب مبتدأ وخبره يضارب فالمعنى : إنَّ المضارب تقعُ منه المضاربة، وأما عدم التنوين فعلى أنه مضاف إلى قوله : المضارب يضارب.
وقوله : يضارب ؛ إمّا صفة لقوله : المضارب أو حال منه، لكن في تقدير الصفة خدشة ظاهرة وهو عدم التطابق بين الموصوف وصفته في التعريف والتنكير؛ لكون الجملة في حكم النكرة، اللّهُمَّ إلا أن يقال : اللام في المضارب للجنس، فيكون بمنزلة النكرة.
وعلى الحالية يراد أنَّ الحال لا تجيء من المضاف إليه إلا في صور ثلاث، وهذا ليس منها ، فالأولى في صورة الإضافة ما في بعض النسخ : باب المضارب الذي يضارب.
[٢]
قوله : ولا يضمن المضارب...الخ ؛ يعني إنَّ المضارب إذا دفع مال المضاربة إلى غيره مضاربة بلا إذن من ربِّ المال فلا ضمان على المضارب إذا هلك المالُ بمجرَّدِ الدفع ما لم يعمل المضارب الثاني في المال، وإذا عمل ضمن الدافع سواء ربح الثاني أو لا. وهذا في ظاهر الرواية عن الإمام، وهو قولهما، وفي رواية الحسن عن الإمام: إنه لا يضمن بالعمل أيضاً ما لم يربح ، وعند زفر: يضمن بالدفع سواء تصرف أو لم يتصرّف، وهو رواية عن أبي يوسف، هو قول الأئمة الثلاثة.
[٣]
بلا إذن إلى أن يعمل الثاني في ظاهر الرواية، وهو قولهما، وإلى أن يربح في رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة، وجه الأول : أنَّ الدفع قبل العمل إيداع ، وهو يملكه، فإذا عمل تبين أنه مضاربة ، فيضمن، وجه الثاني : أنَّ الدفع قبل العمل إيداع، وبعده إبضاع، وهو يملكهما ، فإذا ربح ثبت الشركة، فحينئذ يضمن، كما لو خُلِطَ بغيره.
[٤]
قوله : بلا إذن ؛ كان ينبغي أن يقول : بلا إذن أو تفويض، فإنّه إذا قال ربُّ المال للمضارب : اعمل برأيك، فالمضارب تملك أن يضارب حينئذ. كما صرحوا به.
[٥]
قوله : وجه الأول.... الخ ؛ هذا دليل على ما في ظاهر الرواية. حاصله : إنَّ الدفع حقيقة إيداع ، وله ولاية ذلك، وإنما يثبت كونه للمضاربة إذا صدر العمل من الثاني، فوجب رعاية الحال، والتوقف في الحكم، حتى إذا عمل الثاني وجب الضمان وإلا فلا ، وقد يستدل بأنَّ الرِّبحَ إنّما يحصلُ بالعمل ، فقام بحصولِ الربح مقام حقيقة حصوله في صيرورة المال مضموناً به.
[٦]
قوله : فيضمن ؛ وهذا إذا كانت المضاربتان صحيحتين، وأما إذا كانت إحداهما فاسدة أو كلتاهما ، فلا ضمان على واحد منهما ؛ لأنه إن كانت الثانية الفاسدة صار الثاني أجيراً، وللأوّل أن يستأجرَ مَن يعمل في المال، وإن كانت هي الأولى فكذلك؛ لأنّ فسادها يوجب فساد الثانية ؛ لأنّ الأولى لما فسدت صارَ إجارة، وصار الربح كله لرب المال. ولو صحت الثانية في هذه الحالة لصارَ الثاني شريكاً، وليس للأجير أن يشارك غیره، فكانت فاسدة بالضرورة، وكانا أجيرين، وكذا إذا كانـا فاسدتين ، وإذا كانـا أجيرين لا يضمن واحد منهما. كما صرحوا به.
[٧]
قوله : وجه الثاني.... الخ ؛ هذا استدلال على ما رواه الحسن عن الإمام ، وحاصله : إنّ دفع المضارب الأوّل قبل عمل المضارب الثاني إيداع ، وبعده إبضاع، والفعلان يملكهما المضارب، فلا يضمن بهما إلا أنَّ المضارب الثاني إذا ربح فقد ثبت له شركة في المال، فيضمن لإشراكه الغير في ربح مال رب المال، وهذا كما إذا خلط مالَ المضاربة بغير مالها.
Chapter on the mudarib who gives mudarabah (to another). And the mudarib is not liable for his handing over (the capital) as mudarabah. [1] His saying: Chapter on the mudarib who gives mudarabah; it is well-known that the author, when he finished explaining the simple mudarabah, began explaining the compound, for the compound naturally follows the simple, and thus in arrangement. But there is discussion: because the mudarabah of the mudarib, even though it comes after the mudarabah of the capital owner, is also simple, not compound of two mudarabahs. So it is better to say: when the author finished explaining the ruling of the first mudarabah, he began explaining the ruling of the second mudarabah, for the second always follows the first. And regarding his saying: 'Chapter'; it is permissible to have tanwin or not. With tanwin, it is the predicate of a deleted subject, i.e., 'this'. And his saying: 'the mudarib' is subject, and its predicate is 'gives mudarabah', so the meaning is: mudarabah occurs from the mudarib. Without tanwin, it is added to his saying: 'the mudarib gives mudarabah'. And his saying: 'gives mudarabah' is either an adjective of 'the mudarib' or a circumstantial accusative, but in the adjective estimation there is an apparent flaw, namely the lack of agreement between the described and the adjective in definiteness and indefiniteness, because the sentence is considered indefinite, unless it is said that the lām in 'al-mudarib' is for the genus, so it is like an indefinite. And according to the circumstantial accusative, it is intended that the circumstantial accusative does not come from the annexed except in three forms, and this is not among them, so the better in the annexed form is what is in some copies: 'Chapter on the mudarib who gives mudarabah'. [2] His saying: 'And the mudarib is not liable...' means: the mudarib, when he hands over the capital of the mudarabah to another as mudarabah without permission from the capital owner, there is no liability on the mudarib if the capital is lost merely by handing over, as long as the second mudarib does not work with the capital. And if he works, the one who handed over is liable, whether the second made profit or not. This is in the manifest transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah) from the Imam (Abu Hanifa), and it is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). In a narration from al-Hasan from the Imam, he is not liable by work either, as long as he does not make profit. And according to Zufar, he is liable by handing over whether he acted or not, and this is a narration from Abu Yusuf, and it is the view of the three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad). [3] Without permission until the second works, in the manifest transmission it is the view of the two, and until he profits in the narration of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa. The proof of the first: handing over before work is a deposit, and he has the authority to do that. When he works, it becomes clear that it was mudarabah, so he is liable. The proof of the second: handing over before work is a deposit, and after it is a speculation (ibdaa'), and the mudarib has authority over both. So when he profits, partnership is established, so then he is liable, just as if he mixed it with other capital. [4] His saying: without permission; he should have said: without permission or delegation, because if the capital owner says to the mudarib: act according to your opinion, then the mudarib has the authority to give mudarabah at that time, as they explained. [5] His saying: the proof of the first... this is evidence for what is in the manifest transmission. Its summary: handing over is in reality a deposit, and he has authority over it. Its being mudarabah is only established when work occurs from the second. So it is necessary to observe the situation and suspend the ruling, until the second works, then liability is necessary, otherwise not. And it may be argued that profit is only obtained by work, so the occurrence of profit takes the place of its actual occurrence in making the capital liable. [6] His saying: so he is liable; this is if both mudarabahs are valid. If one of them is invalid or both, then neither is liable. Because if the second is invalid, the second becomes an employee, and the first may hire someone to work with the capital. If the first is invalid, it is similar, because its invalidity necessitates the invalidity of the second; because when the first becomes invalid, it becomes a hire, and all profit goes to the capital owner. And if the second were valid in this situation, the second would become a partner, but an employee cannot partner with another, so it is necessarily invalid, and both become employees. Similarly if both are invalid. And when both are employees, neither is liable, as they explained. [7] His saying: the proof of the second... this is a proof for what al-Hasan narrated from the Imam. Its summary: the handing over by the first mudarib before the work of the second mudarib is a deposit, and after it is a speculation, and the mudarib has authority over both actions, so he is not liable due to them unless the second mudarib profits, then partnership in the capital is established, so he is liable because he involved another in the profit of the capital owner's capital. And this is like when he mixes mudarabah capital with other capital.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage from Sharh al-Wiqayah discusses the ruling on a mudarib (working partner) who sub-contracts the mudarabah capital to another mudarib without the capital owner's permission. The base text states: 'The mudarib is not liable merely by handing over the capital as mudarabah.' The commentator then explains the different positions within the Hanafi school. In the Zahir al-Riwayah (the six core books of Imam Muhammad), the ruling is that the first mudarib is not liable for the capital simply by handing it over; liability only attaches when the second mudarib actually works with the capital. This is also the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). However, there is a narration from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa that liability does not attach even after work until profit is earned. Zufar holds that liability attaches immediately upon handing over, regardless of any subsequent action. The commentator then provides the legal reasoning (wajh) for each view. For the Zahir al-Riwayah view: handing over before work is a deposit (wadi'ah), which the mudarib is entitled to do. Work transforms it into mudarabah, so liability follows work. For the Hasan narration: before work it is a deposit, after work it is a speculation (ibdaa'), both permissible. Only when profit is earned does the second mudarib become a partner, triggering liability for involving an outsider in the profit of the capital owner's property. The commentator adds that these rulings apply when both mudarabahs are valid. If either is invalid (fasid), the parties become employees (ajir), and no liability for loss arises. This passage highlights the nuanced ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school on the point at which a mudarib becomes liable for sub-contracting, with the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position being the Zahir al-Riwayah view: liability upon work, not merely handing over.

Key Terms
مضارب (mudārib): The working partner in a mudarabah contract who manages the capital.
مضاربة (muḍārabah): A partnership contract where one party provides capital and the other provides labor, with profit shared according to agreement.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability to compensate for loss or damage to the capital due to transgression or unauthorized action.
إيداع (īdāʿ): Deposit; a contract where property is entrusted to another for safekeeping without liability for loss unless negligence.
إبضاع (ibḍāʿ): Speculation; a transaction where one gives capital to another to trade with, but without the profit-sharing structure of mudarabah (more like a loan or commission).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Zahir al-Riwayah (manifest transmission) in the Hanafi school, when does a mudarib become liable for sub-contracting mudarabah capital without the capital owner's permission?
A) As soon as he hands over the capital to the second mudarib.
B) When the second mudarib works with the capital.
C) Only when the second mudarib earns a profit.
D) Never, because the mudarib has full authority to delegate.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a mudarib who sub-contracts without permission is liable only when the second mudarib works with the capital, not upon handing over or upon profit.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
advanced
12 min
The Mudarib's Liability When Delegating Without Permission: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability trigger and its consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the trigger of liability (work, profit, or delivery) and apply the ẓāhir al-riwāyah position to determine the owner's options and the purity of profit.

Core Idea
Liability triggers upon work (Sahibayn), not delivery or profit—the relied-upon view.

This passage from ʿUmdat al-Riʿāyah examines a critical scenario in muḍārabah: the first mudarib gives the capital to a second without the owner's permission. When does he become liable? The school contains three views, with the ẓāhir al-riwāyah position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad being the operative one. Understanding this dispute clarifies not only liability but also the owner's choices and the purity of profit earned.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
State each position on when liability attaches: upon work of the second (Sahibayn), upon profit (Imam via Hasan), upon delivery (Zufar).
The ẓāhir al-riwāyah is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
2
Analyze the reasoning
For each, explain the legal basis: delivery as deposit, work as mudarabah, profit as partnership. Note the qiyas to deposit.
The qiyas panel in the toolbox details the analogy.
3
Apply the condition of valid contracts
Liability only arises if both muḍārabahs are valid; if invalid, no liability and parties become employees.
See the text's discussion of fāsid contracts.
4
Examine the owner's options
The owner may hold the first or second liable, but cannot take profit without liability. Explain the effect of each choice.
The well-known narration (al-riwāyah al-mashhūrah) provides these options.
5
Determine the purity of profit
The second's profit is halal; the first's must be given in charity due to retrospective ownership via liability.
The text compares to the case of mūdaʿ al-mūdaʿ.

Source Text

بلا إذن إلى أن يعمل الثاني في ظاهر الرواية، وهو قولهما، وإلى أن يربح في رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة. وجه الأول: أن الدفع قبل العمل إيداع، وهو يملكه، فإذا عمل تبين أنه مضاربة، فيضمن. وجه الثاني: أن الدفع قبل العمل إيداع، وبعده إبضاع، وهو يملكهما، فإذا ربح ثبت الشركة، فحينئذ يضمن، كما لو خلط بغيره. [١] قوله: بلا إذن؛ كان ينبغي أن يقول: بلا إذن أو تفويض، فإنه إذا قال رب المال للمضارب: اعمل برأيك، فالمضارب تملك أن يضارب حينئذ. كما صرحوا به. [٢] قوله: وجه الأول... الخ؛ هذا دليل على ما في ظاهر الرواية. حاصله: إن الدفع حقيقة إيداع، وله ولاية ذلك، وإنما يثبت كونه للمضاربة إذا صدر العمل من الثاني، فوجب رعاية الحال، والتوقف في الحكم، حتى إذا عمل الثاني وجب الضمان وإلا فلا، وقد يستدل بأن الربح إنما يحصل بالعمل، فقام بحصول الربح مقام حقيقة حصوله في صيرورة المال مضمونا به. [٣] قوله: فيضمن؛ وهذا إذا كانت المضاربتان صحيحتين، وأما إذا كانت إحداهما فاسدة أو كلتاهما، فلا ضمان على واحد منهما؛ لأنه إن كانت الثانية الفاسدة صار الثاني أجيراً، وللأول أن يستأجر من يعمل في المال، وإن كانت هي الأولى فكذلك؛ لأن فسادها يوجب فساد الثانية؛ لأن الأولى لما فسدت صارت إجارة، وصار الربح كله لرب المال. ولو صحت الثانية في هذه الحالة لصار الثاني شريكاً، وليس للأجير أن يشارك غيره، فكانت فاسدة بالضرورة، وكانا أجيرين، وكذا إذا كانتا فاسدتين، وإذا كانا أجيرين لا يضمن واحد منهما. كما صرحوا به. [٤] قوله: وجه الثاني... الخ؛ هذا استدلال على ما رواه الحسن عن الإمام، وحاصله: إن دفع المضارب الأول قبل عمل المضارب الثاني إيداع، وبعده إبضاع، والفعلان يملكهما المضارب، فلا يضمن بهما إلا أن المضارب الثاني إذا ربح فقد ثبت له شركة في المال، فيضمن لإشراكه الغير في ربح مال رب المال، وهذا كما إذا خلط مال المضاربة بغير مالها. وعند زفره: يضمن بمجرد الدفع. ثم اعلم أن الضمان لما وجب بعمل المضارب الثاني في ظاهر الرواية، وبالربح في رواية الحسن عن الإمام. ففي الرواية المشهورة فيه: رب المال إن شاء ضمن المضارب الأول رأس ماله؛ لتعديه عليه، وإن شاء ضمن الثاني لقبضه بغير إذن المالك، وإن اختار رب المال أن يأخذ الربح ولا يضمن ليس له ذلك، فإن ضمن الأول صحت المضاربة بينه وبين الثاني؛ لأنه ملكه بالضمان من حين خالف بالدفع إلى غيره لا على الوجه الذي رضي به، فصار كما إذا دفع مال نفسه، وكان الربح على ما شرط. وإن ضمن الثاني رجع مما ضمن على الأول بالعقد؛ لأنه عامل له كالمودع، ولأنه مغرور من جهة في ضمن العقد، وصحت المضاربة بينهما، ويكون الربح بينهما على ما شرطا، ويطيب للثاني ما ربح؛ لأنه يستحقه بالعمل. ولا خبث في العمل، ولا يطيب للأول لأنه يستحقه بملكه المستند بأداء الضمان؛ لأنه يستحقه برأس المال، والملك في رأس المال حصل بأداء الضمان مستندا، ولا يعرى عن نوع خبث؛ لأنه ثابت من وجه دون وجه، فمن حيث أنه لا ملك له تمكن الخبث فيه، فيكون سبيله التصدق. وقيل: على الخلاف في إيداع المودع، فيضمن الأول فقط، ولا يضمن الثاني عند الإمام، وعندهما يضمن بناء على اختلافهم في مودع المودع، فإن عنده: لا يضمن، وعندهما: يتخير. والفرق بينهما للإمام أن مودع المودع كان يقبضه لنفع الأول فلا يكون ضامنا؛ لأن على الأول حفظه الوديعة، فإذا دفع إلى غيره يكون الثاني عاقلا له بأمره في القبض، فينتقل عمله إلى الأول، فصار كأنه حفظ بنفسه. ولو هلك في يد الأول لا يجب الضمان، وكذا إذا هلك في يد الثاني، وأما المضارب الثاني فعامل لنفسه في القبض؛ لأنه لم يكتسبه إلا لتحصيل الربح لنفسه، فلا ينتقل عمله إلى الأول. كما في شروح «الهداية» و«الكنز»). [1] قوله: يضمن بمجرد الدفع؛ لأن الذي يمكنه المضارب الأول هو الدفع على (۱) ينظر: «التبيين (٥ : ٦٤).
Without permission until the second works in the apparent narration, which is their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's) statement, and until he profits in the narration of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa. The basis of the first: that the payment before work is a deposit, and he owns it, so when he works it becomes clear that it is a mudarabah, so he is liable. The basis of the second: that the payment before work is a deposit, and after it is a commission, and he owns both, so when profit occurs the partnership is established, then he is liable, just as if he mixed it with other property. [1] His statement: 'without permission'; it would be appropriate to say 'without permission or delegation', because if the owner says to the mudarib: 'act on your own opinion', then the mudarib has the right to enter into a mudarabah then. As they explicitly stated. [2] His statement: 'the basis of the first...' etc.; this is evidence for what is in the apparent narration. Its summary: that the payment is in reality a deposit, and he has authority over that, and its being for mudarabah is established only when work issues from the second, so consideration of the situation is required, and suspension of the ruling, until when the second works, liability is obligated, otherwise not. And it may be inferred that profit is only obtained by work, so the occurrence of profit takes the place of the actual occurrence [of work] in making the property guaranteed. [3] His statement: 'so he is liable'; and this is when both mudarabahs are valid. But if one of them is invalid or both, there is no liability on either of them; because if the second is invalid, the second becomes an employee, and the first may hire someone to work with the capital. If the first is invalid, likewise; because its invalidity necessitates the invalidity of the second; because when the first became invalid, it became a hire, and all profit belongs to the owner. If the second were valid in this case, the second would become a partner, and an employee may not partner with others, so it is necessarily invalid, and both are employees. Likewise if both are invalid. And when both are employees, neither is liable. As they explicitly stated. [4] His statement: 'the basis of the second...' etc.; this is an argument for what al-Hasan narrated from the Imam, and its summary: that the payment of the first mudarib before the work of the second mudarib is a deposit, and after it is a commission, and the mudarib owns both actions, so he is not liable by them except that when the second mudarib makes a profit, partnership in the property is established for him, so he is liable because he caused another to share in the profit of the owner's property. And this is like when he mixes the capital of mudarabah with other property. And according to Zufar: he is liable by mere payment. Then know that liability is obligated by the work of the second mudarib in the apparent narration, and by profit in the narration of al-Hasan from the Imam. So in the well-known narration concerning it: the owner, if he wishes, may hold the first mudarib liable for the capital because of his transgression, and if he wishes may hold the second liable for his taking without the owner's permission. And if the owner chooses to take the profit and not hold anyone liable, he does not have that. If he holds the first liable, the mudarabah between him and the second is valid; because he owns the capital by liability from the time he deviated by paying to another not in the manner he consented to, so it becomes as if he paid his own property, and the profit is as agreed. If he holds the second liable, the second may recourse for what he was liable for against the first by contract; because he is his agent like a depositee, and because he is deceived by him, so it is included in the contract, and the mudarabah between them is valid, and the profit is between them as agreed. What the second earned is pure (halal) because he deserves it by work. There is no impurity in the work. But for the first, it is not pure because he deserves it by ownership based on payment of liability; because he deserves it by the capital, and ownership of the capital occurred by payment of liability retrospectively, and it is not free from a kind of impurity because it is established from one aspect but not another. From the standpoint that he has no ownership, impurity is possible in it, so its way is to give it in charity. And it is said: on the disagreement in the deposit of a depositee: the first is liable only, and the second is not liable according to the Imam; according to them both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he is liable, based on their disagreement concerning the depositee of a depositee. Indeed, according to him, he is not liable; according to them, he has the choice. The difference between them according to the Imam is that the depositee of a depositee takes possession for the benefit of the first, so he is not liable; because the first is obliged to protect the deposit. If he pays to another, the second acts as an agent for him in taking possession by his order, so his work transfers to the first, and it becomes as if he preserved it himself. If it perishes in the hand of the first, liability is not obligated; likewise if it perishes in the hand of the second. As for the second mudarib, he acts for himself in taking possession; because he acquires it only to obtain profit for himself, so his work does not transfer to the first. As in the commentaries of al-Hidayah and al-Kanz. [1] His statement: 'he is liable by mere payment'; because what the first mudarib can do is payment.(1) See: al-Tabyin (5:64).
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the liability (damān) of a mudarib who hands over the mudarabah capital to another mudarib without the owner's permission. The core issue is when the first mudarib becomes liable (dāmin) for the capital. The text presents three positions. The first position, which is the zāhir al-riwāyah (the apparent transmission from the six core books of Imam Muhammad) and the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sāhibayn), states that the first mudarib becomes liable only when the second mudarib begins to work with the capital. Their reasoning is that the delivery before work is a deposit (īdā‘), which the first mudarib is authorized to make. Once the second works, it becomes clear that it was a mudarabah, and thus liability attaches. The second position, narrated by Hasan ibn Ziyād from Imam Abu Hanifa, holds that liability arises only when the second mudarib makes a profit. Their argument: the initial delivery is a deposit, and after work it becomes a commission (ibḍā‘); both actions are within the mudarib's authority. Liability only arises upon profit because that establishes a partnership in the profit, akin to mixing the capital with other property. The third position, attributed to Zufar, is that liability occurs immediately upon mere delivery. The text then discusses when the contracts are invalid (fāsid). If either or both mudarabahs are invalid, neither mudarib is liable; they become employees (ajīr). Next, the commentary explains the well-known narration (al-riwāyah al-mashhūrah): the owner has the option to hold either the first or the second mudarib liable for the principal, but cannot take the profit without holding anyone liable. If the owner holds the first liable, the mudarabah between the first and second becomes valid as if the first had used his own capital, and the profit is divided as agreed. If he holds the second liable, the second can recourse against the first. The profit earned by the second is pure (ḥalāl), but the first's profit is impure and must be given in charity due to the retrospective ownership through liability. Finally, the text compares this to the case of a depositee (mūda‘) who deposits with another (mūda‘ al-mūda‘). In that case, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, only the first is liable and the second is not; according to the Sāhibayn, the owner has a choice. The difference is that the sub-depositee takes possession for the benefit of the first depositee, so his work transfers to the first, whereas the second mudarib works for himself. This passage is a detailed expansion of the base text (al-Wiqāyah) by the commentator, providing proofs, hypothetical scenarios, and cross-references to other Hanafi works like al-Hidāyah and al-Kanz.

Key Terms
مضاربة (muḍārabah): A contract of profit-sharing whereby one party (rabb al-māl) provides capital and the other (muḍārib) provides labor, with profit shared as agreed and loss borne by the capital provider.
إيداع (īdā‘): Deposit — entrusting property to another for safekeeping without authorization to use it.
إبضاع (ibḍā‘): Commission — entrusting property to another to trade with it on behalf of the owner, without sharing in profit (the agent is paid or works for free).
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability/guarantee — obligation to compensate for loss or damage to property. In this context, it refers to the first mudarib becoming liable for the capital.
ظاهر الرواية (ẓāhir al-riwāyah): The apparent/dominant narration — rulings transmitted in the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (al-Mabsūṭ, al-Jāmi‘ al-Ṣaghīr, al-Jāmi‘ al-Kabīr, al-Siyar al-Ṣaghīr, al-Siyar al-Kabīr, al-Ziyādāt). These are the most authoritative in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the ẓāhir al-riwāyah (the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), when does the first mudarib become liable (ḍāmin) if he gives the capital to a second mudarib without permission?
A) Immediately upon delivery.
B) When the second mudarib begins working.
C) When the second mudarib makes a profit.
D) Never, unless the owner chooses.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a mudarib who delegates without permission becomes liable for the capital once the second mudarib starts working (Sahibayn), and the owner may choose to hold either liable, but the second's profit is pure while the first's is not.

Profit Distribution in Sub-Mudarabah: Two Cases of Owner's Wording
Ruling on profit shares when first mudarib engages second mudarib with owner's permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the profit shares when the owner permits a sub-mudarabah and stipulates 'half of what Allah provides' either generally or specifically to the first mudarib.

Core Idea
The first mudarib's share is residual after paying owner and second mudarib; wording determines whether owner shares only the first mudarib's profit.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya expands on a mudarabah scenario where the owner permits the first mudarib to engage a second mudarib with part of the capital. The key variable is the phrasing of the profit-sharing condition between owner and first mudarib. By working through two subcases, you will see how the first mudarib's share is computed as a residual after deducting the owner's and second mudarib's agreed shares, supported by a qiyas to sub-hiring.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Note the owner's wording: (1) 'What Allah provides between us halves' (general), (2) 'What Allah provides you (O mudarib) between us halves' (specific to first mudarib's profit).
The second scenario restricts the owner's share to only the profit earned by the first mudarib.
2
List the profit shares
For each scenario, state the shares: owner, first mudarib, second mudarib. In scenario 1: owner 1/2, first mudarib 1/6, second mudarib 1/3. In scenario 2: each gets 1/3.
The second mudarib always gets 1/3 as agreed with the first mudarib.
3
Explain the reasoning
The first mudarib's share is what remains after deducting the owner's share and the second mudarib's share. Since the owner's half is fixed, the second mudarib's 1/3 comes from the first mudarib's half, leaving him 1/6. In scenario 2, the owner's half is only half of the first mudarib's profit (2/3 of total), so owner gets 1/3, first mudarib gets 1/3, and second mudarib gets 1/3.
The first mudarib cannot reduce the owner's share; the second mudarib's share is deducted from the first mudarib's entitlement.
4
Understand the qiyas to hiring
The commentary draws an analogy: if Zaid hires a tailor to sew a garment for 1 dirham, and the tailor sub-hires another for 1/2 dirham, the first tailor gets 1/2 dirham. Similarly, the first mudarib's profit is the residual after paying the second mudarib.
The qiyas establishes that the action of the second is attributed to the first, so the first's share is what remains.
5
Apply to a numerical example
Take total profit = 120. Scenario 1: owner 60, second 40, first 20. Scenario 2: each gets 40.
Practice the calculation by varying the profit amount.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلو أذنَ بالدفع فدفع بالثلث ، وقيل له : ما رَزَقَ اللهُ تعالى بيننا نصفان ، فنصف ربحه للمالك، وسدسه للأول، وثلثه للثاني، وإن قيل له : ما رزقك الله تعالى، فلكل ثلث (فلو أذن بالدفع فدفع بالثلث ، وقيل له : ما رَزَقَ الله تعالى بيننا نصفان ، فنصف ربحه للمالك، وسدسَهُ للأَوّل، وثلثه للثاني ، وإن قيل له: ما رزقك الله تعالى، فلكل ثلث) ؛ لأن المالك" قد أذن بالدفع مضاربة، فللمضارب الثاني ما شَرَطَ له المضاربُ الأَوَّل، فما رزق اللهُ المضارب الأول، وهو الثلثان يكون نصفين بينه وبين رب المال. وجه للإيداع ، وهذا الدفع على وجه المضاربة، فصار مخالفاً، فيضمن لا محالة. [١] قوله : فلو أذن ...الخ ؛ يعني لو أذنَ ربُّ المال للمضارب بالدفع إلى آخر بالمضاربة، فضارب المضارب بالثلث، وكان رب المال قال للمضارب الأوّل: ما رزق الله بيننا نصفان، فعمل الثاني وربح فنصف الربح لرب المال، وسدسه للمضارب الأول، وثلثه للمضارب الثاني ؛ لأنَّ الدفع إلى المضارب الثاني مضاربة ؛ لأنه كان بإذنِ المالك. شيئاً، وقد شرط لنفسه نصف جميع ما رزق الله تعالى، وقد جعل المضارب الأول للثاني ثلثه ، فينصرف ذلك إلى نصيبه ؛ لأنه لا يقدر على أن ينقص من نصيب رب المال ، فبقي للأول السدس. ويطيب ذلك الربح للكل ؛ لأنَّ رب المال يستحقه بالمال، وهما بالعمل، وإن كان المضاربُ الأول لم يعمل شيئاً بنفسه، لكن وقع له فعل الثاني، كما إذا استأجر زيد على خياطة ثوب بدرهم، فاستأجر غيره على عمل الخياطة بنصف درهم. [٢] قوله : وإن قيل له...الخ ؛ يعني وإن قال ربُّ المال للمضارب الأول : ما رزقك الله فهو بيننا نصفان، فلكل من ربِّ المال والمضارب الأول والثاني ثلث الربح. [٣] قوله : لأن المالك ... الخ ؛ حاصله : إنّ ربَّ المالِ فوَّض التصرّف إلى المضارب الأول، وجعل لنفسه نصف ما رزق المضاربُ الأوّل، وهو رزق الثلثين ، فهذان الثلثان يكونان بين رب المال والمضارب الأول نصفين.
So if he (the owner) permitted the [first] mudarib to give [the capital] to another, and he gave one third [of the capital to a second mudarib], and it was said to him [by the owner]: 'What Allah provides is between us halves', then half of the profit is for the owner, one sixth for the first [mudarib], and one third for the second. And if it was said to him: 'What Allah provides you [O mudarib] is between us halves', then each gets one third. (The matn repeats this). Because the owner permitted the giving as mudarabah, so for the second mudarib what the first mudarib stipulated for him. So what Allah provided the first mudarib, which is two thirds, becomes halves between him and the owner. [It is as if it were] a deposit, but this giving is on the basis of mudarabah, so it is contrary [to the permission] and he guarantees [the capital] inevitably. [1] His saying: 'So if he permitted...etc.' means: if the owner permitted the first mudarib to give [the capital] to another as mudarabah, and the first mudarib engaged [the second] with one third [of the capital], and the owner had said to the first mudarib: 'What Allah provides between us halves', then the second worked and made profit, so half the profit is for the owner, one sixth for the first mudarib, and one third for the second mudarib. Because the giving to the second mudarib is mudarabah, since it was with the owner's permission. And [the first mudarib] had stipulated for himself half of all that Allah provided, and the first mudarib gave the second one third of it, so that [one third] is deducted from his own share, because he cannot reduce the owner's share. So one sixth remains for the first. And this profit is lawful (halal) for all; because the owner deserves it for the capital, and they [the mudaribs] for the work, even if the first mudarib did not work himself, but the action of the second is attributed to him, like if Zaid hires someone to sew a garment for a dirham, and that person hires another to do the sewing for half a dirham. [2] His saying: 'And if it was said to him...etc.' means: if the owner said to the first mudarib: 'What Allah provides you is between us halves', then each of the owner, the first mudarib, and the second mudarib gets one third of the profit. [3] His saying: 'Because the owner...etc.' Summary: The owner delegated disposal [of the capital] to the first mudarib, and stipulated for himself half of what the first mudarib earns, which is the profit from two thirds [of the capital]. So these two thirds are halves between the owner and the first mudarib.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage presents two scenarios of profit distribution when the owner permits the first mudarib to invest part of the capital with a second mudarib, and the profit-sharing condition between owner and first mudarib is phrased differently. In both scenarios, the first mudarib invests one third of the capital with a second mudarib. The passage is a commentary (sharh) that expands the ruling of the matn. The first scenario: the owner says 'What Allah provides (through this mudarabah) is between us halves.' The total profit: owner gets half, second mudarib gets one third (as agreed with first mudarib), and the first mudarib gets one sixth. The reasoning: The first mudarib stipulated half of the total profit for himself, but he gave one third of the profit to the second mudarib. Since he cannot reduce the owner's half, the one third comes out of his own share (half), leaving him one sixth. The second scenario: the owner says 'What Allah provides you (O mudarib) is between us halves.' Here, the owner's share is half of the profit earned by the first mudarib, but since the first mudarib's profit is only two thirds (because one third belongs to the second mudarib), the owner gets half of those two thirds, i.e., one third of total profit. The first mudarib gets one third (his share of the two thirds after giving half to owner), and the second mudarib gets one third. The commentary uses an analogy to hiring: if someone hires a tailor for a dirham and the tailor sub-hires another for half a dirham, the first tailor gets half a dirham. Similarly, the first mudarib gets the residual profit after paying the second mudarib and the owner.

Key Terms
رب المال (rabb al-māl): The owner of the capital who invests it in mudarabah.
المضارب (al-muḍārib): The person who receives capital to trade and shares in profit.
الربح (al-ribḥ): The profit generated from the mudarabah investment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 60 dirhams
B) 40 dirhams
C) 20 dirhams
D) 30 dirhams

Key Takeaway
The first mudarib's profit share is residual after satisfying the owner and the second mudarib's shares, based on the agreed conditions.
