Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a mudarib buys from the capital owner for murabaha, the cost basis includes half of the owner's profit from his original purchase.

The Mudarib's Murabahah: Stating the Lower Price
Commentary on murabahah pricing rules for mudarib buying from capital owner

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the mudarib must state the lower of two prices in a murabahah sale when purchasing from the capital owner and explain the rationale based on trust and shubhat al-adam.

Core Idea
In murabahah, trust demands transparency; the mudarib must disclose the lowest possible cost.

This passage from a Hanafi commentary explains a critical ruling in mudarabah operations: when a mudarib (agent) purchases an item from the capital owner (rabb al-mal) and then resells it on a murabahah (cost-plus) basis, what price should he declare? The commentator highlights that despite the sale being valid, the trust-based nature of murabahah requires the mudarib to state the lower of the two possible prices—the actual cost to him—to avoid any semblance of untrustworthiness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transaction
Note the parties: the mudarib (agent) buys an item from the capital owner (rabb al-mal) using mudarabah capital, then sells it on murabahah. Recognize the two contracts: a sale from rabb al-mal to mudarib, and a murabahah sale from mudarib to a third party.
The purchase price from rabb al-mal is the stated amount (e.g., 1000), but the mudarib's actual cost is lower because he is part owner of the capital.
2
Understand the trust nature of murabahah
Murabahah is a trust-based contract (عقد أمانة). The seller must disclose the true cost price. Any doubt or suspicion of dishonesty invalidates the trust element. Therefore, the contract must be kept free from even a semblance (shubha) of betrayal.
Hanafis treat murabahah as a commutation of trust; thus, ambiguity is strictly avoided.
3
Recognize the shubha (semblance) in this transaction
The sale between mudarib and rabb al-mal is valid but has a 'semblance of non-occurrence' (شبهة العدم) because the mudarib is selling property that still partially belongs to the rabb al-mal. This doubt prevents full reliance on the validity of the second contract.
The higher price (the full purchase price) would imply the contract was fully valid, but due to shubha, the lower price is the safest.
4
Apply the rule of the lower price
Because of the shubha, the mudarib must base his murabahah disclosure on the lower of the two possible prices: the actual cost to him (e.g., 500 in the example). The higher price (1000) is not fully established from all angles.
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school, supported by later authorities like al-Isbijabi, al-Tahtawi, and al-Inayah.
5
Confirm the practical consequence
The mudarib states to the buyer: 'This cost me 500' (the lower price), not 1000. This upholds the trust element. The profit is calculated on 500, and any excess is not permissible.
This ruling applies specifically when the mudarib buys from the rabb al-mal; if buying from a third party, the actual purchase price is stated.

Source Text

Cream of the End for the Cream of the Care. If it was sold for its double, then its share is three thousand, and the profit from it is half a thousand between them. And if he bought from the capital owner for a thousand a slave, he bought it at half of it. (If it was sold for its double, then its share is three thousand, and the profit from it is half a thousand between them): meaning if it was sold for four thousand, then three thousand is the share of the mudarabah, and the thousand is the property of the mudarib specifically. Then the three thousand: from it is paid the capital, which is two thousand five hundred. Then the profit remaining is five hundred, half of it for the capital owner and half for the mudarib. And if he bought from the capital owner for a thousand a slave, he bought it at half of it. The mudarib owns five hundred, and three quarters of it belongs to the owner, which is one thousand five hundred. And the share of the mudarib, which is the quarter, is removed from the mudarabah because his share is guaranteed against him, while the mudarabah capital is a trust. And it is apparent that between being something and being a trust there is contradiction; because if the mudarib's share were not removed from the mudarabah, guarantee would be combined with being a trust, and that is not permissible. And three quarters of the slave remain in the mudarabah because there is nothing in it contrary to mudarabah; because the capital owner is the principal, and the guarantee is only upon the principal. [1] His statement: 'its share...etc.' means the share of the mudarabah is three thousand after the mudarib removes his share which is one thousand; because when he guaranteed a quarter of the slave, his quarter becomes his exclusive property. So the thousand is its price because it is based on four thousand. Then from it the capital is removed, which is two thousand five hundred. [2] His statement: 'and the profit from it...etc.' means the profit from it is five hundred, between the mudarib and the capital owner, so each gets two hundred and fifty. [3] His statement: 'a slave' means a slave whose value is one thousand, so the price and value are equal. We only said that because if there were extra in them, such as the capital owner buying a slave worth two thousand and selling it to the mudarib for two thousand after the mudarib has worked with his thousand in the mudarabah and earned a thousand profit in it, then he sells it at a cost-plus profit on the mudarib's share of one thousand five hundred. But if the mudarabah capital is two thousand, it is like the first case. Similarly, if there is extra in the value of the sold item without extra in the price, such as the slave being worth one thousand five hundred and the capital owner bought it for one thousand and sold it to the mudarib for one thousand, the mudarib sells it at cost-plus profit on one thousand two hundred and fifty. The opposite of this [image omitted] is in the ruling, like the author's case. This was mentioned by Allamah al-Tahtawi in his gloss on al-Durr al-Mukhtar. [1] His statement: 'profiting by half of it' because the contract of murabahah is a trust contract, so it must be kept free from betrayal and from any semblance of betrayal. The first contract occurred for the capital owner, and the second likewise because the mudarib's purchase does not remove it from the ownership of the capital owner. However, the contract was valid for an additional benefit, which is the establishment of possession and disposal for the mudarib. Thus, there remains a semblance of the non-occurrence of the second contract. So he sells it at cost-plus profit based on the first price, which is five hundred. This was mentioned by al-Isbijabi and others. [2] His statement: 'although it is valid' due to differing objectives; because the capital owner's purpose is to obtain the thousand, and the mudarib's purpose is to obtain the sold item, so it meets a need, even though it is a sale of the capital owner's property for his own property. [3] His statement: 'so the lower of the two prices is considered' which is five hundred because it is established from all angles, while the higher is established from one angle but not another, considering that it is a sale of his property for his property. This is in al-Inayah. [4] His statement: 'And if he bought with her thousand a slave...' means that if the mudarib with half shares bought with the thousand of mudarabah a slave worth two thousand, and that slave killed a man by mistake, and they were ordered to hand over or ransom, then if they hand over the slave to the victim's guardian, the mudarabah ends due to the loss of its capital without compensation. Similarly, if they ransom, the slave leaves the mudarabah.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on the rulings of mudarabah when the mudarib (agent) sells goods on a murabahah (cost-plus-profit) basis. The author first explains a scenario where the mudarabah capital is 2,500 and goods are sold for double (4,000). The profit is 500 split equally between capital owner and mudarib. Then a key ruling is introduced: if the mudarib buys a slave from the capital owner for 1,000, the purchase price is considered half of the capital (500) for murabahah purposes. The commentary clarifies that the mudarib's share in the purchased item must be removed from the mudarabah capital because his guaranteed share cannot coexist with trust property. Three-fourths of the item remains in the mudarabah. Further notes explain that in murabahah, the lower of the two prices (the actual cost to the mudarib) must be stated, because murabahah is a trust-based contract and must be free from any suspicion of treachery. Even though the contract of sale between mudarib and capital owner is valid, it has a semblance of invalidity, so the mudarib must disclose the lowest possible cost. The passage also discusses variations in value and price, and ends with a scenario where the purchased slave is killed accidentally and the mudarabah ends upon compensation.

Key Terms
المضاربة (al-muḍārabah): A partnership where capital is provided by one party (rabb al-mal) and labor by another (mudarib), with profit sharing as agreed.
المرابحة (al-murābaḥah): A sale where the seller discloses the cost price and adds a stated profit; considered a trust-based contract.
رب المال (rabb al-māl): The capital provider in a mudarabah partnership.
المضارب (al-muḍārib): The labor provider in a mudarabah; the agent who trades with the capital.
أمانة (amānah): Trust; property held without liability for loss except in case of negligence.
شبهة العدم (shubhat al-ʿadam): A semblance of non-existence or invalidity in a contract; a doubt that prevents full reliance on the contract's validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why must the mudarib state the lower of two prices in a murabahah sale when he bought the item from the capital owner?
A) Because the higher price is usurious.
B) Because murabahah is a trust contract and there is a semblance of invalidity (shubhat al-adam) in the initial purchase.
C) Because the capital owner forbids stating the higher price.
D) Because the mudarib does not own the item.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a mudarib selling on murabahah goods bought from the capital owner must state the lower of the two possible prices due to the trust nature of murabahah and the shubhat al-adam in the initial transaction.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing

Murabahah Sale by Mudarib: The Lower Price Principle
Explains murabahah cost when mudarib buys from capital owner

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the price a mudarib must declare in a murabahah sale when the slave was purchased from the capital owner, and explain the Hanafi reasoning (shubhat al-ʿadam) behind it.

Core Idea
In murabahah, the mudarib must declare the lower of two possible prices to avoid any semblance of dishonesty.

Imagine a mudarib who buys a slave from the capital owner himself using part of the capital. The slave is profitable, but when the mudarib wants to sell it as murabahah, he must decide what cost to disclose. This passage explains that due to a subtle legal doubt (shubhat al-ʿadam), the purchase from the capital owner is not a true transfer of ownership, so the mudarib must report only the lower price. This ruling upholds the trust-based nature of murabahah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract parties and sequence
The capital owner (rabb al-mal) initially buys a slave for 1000 dirhams, then the mudarib purchases that same slave from the capital owner for 500 dirhams (half the capital). The mudarib now wants to sell the slave on murabahah.
2
Recognize the trust basis of murabahah
Murabahah is a 'trust contract' (aqd amanah); the seller must disclose the exact cost and be free from any suspicion of dishonesty.
Any doubt (shubhah) about the cost must be avoided.
3
Understand the concept of shubhat al-'adam
The purchase by the mudarib from the capital owner is valid only to give the mudarib control, but it does not truly transfer ownership—it's a sale of one's own property to oneself in effect. Thus there is a 'semblance of non-existence' (shubhat al-'adam) regarding the second sale.
This doubt makes the higher price (1000) uncertain.
4
Apply the principle of the lower price
Because murabahah requires certainty, the mudarib must use the lower price (500) which is established from every angle. The larger amount (1000) is established only partially and is therefore unreliable.
The ruling is based on istihsan to preserve trust.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المضاربة المضارب الذي يضارب رابح بنصفه، ولو شَرَى بألفها عبداً رابح بنصفه ) ، فقولُهُ: شراهُ بنصفه صفةُ العبد، وضمير الفاعل في شراء يرجعُ إلى ربِّ المال، فالمضارب إن باعَهُ مرابحة يقولُ : قامَ علي بنصف الألف ؛ لأنَّ شراءَ المضارب من رب المال وإن كان جائزاً ففيه شُبهة العدم، ومبنى المرابحة على الأمانة، فيعتبر أقل الثّمنين". (ولو شَرَى بألفها عبداً الصورة في الحكم، كمسألة المصنف . ذكره العلامة الطحطاوي في حاشيته على الدر المختار»). [١] قوله : رابح بنصفه ؛ لأنَّ عقد المرابحة عقد ،أمانة، فيجب تنزيهه عن الخيانة، وعن شبهة الخيانة، والعقد الأوّل وقع لرب المال، والثاني كذلك ؛ لأنّ شراء المضارب لا يخرج عن ملك ربِّ المال. إلا أنه صح العقد لزيادة فائدة، وهي ثبوت اليد والتصرف للمضارب، فبقي شبهة عدم وقوع العقد الثاني، فيبيعه مرابحة على الثمن الأول، وذلك خمسمئة، ذكره الاسيجابي، وغيره" [٢] قوله : وإن كان جائزاً لتغاير المقاصد ؛ لأنَّ مقصود رب المال وصوله إلى الألف، ومقصود المضارب وصوله إلى المبيع، ففيه دفع للحاجة، وإن كان بيع ملكِ رب المال بملكه. [٣] قوله : فيعتبر أقل الثمنين ؛ وهو خمسمئة لثبوتِهِ من كل وجه، والأكثر ثابت من وجه دون وجه ، بالنظر إلى أنه بيع ماله بماله. كذا في «العناية».

So his statement: 'he bought it by half of it' is a description of the slave, and the pronoun of the agent in 'he bought' refers to the capital owner. So if the mudarib sells it as murabahah, he says: 'it cost me half of the thousand'; because the mudarib's purchase from the capital owner, although permissible, has a semblance of non-existence, and murabahah is based on trust, so the lower of the two prices is considered. The first contract occurred for the capital owner, and the second likewise, because the mudarib's purchase does not take it out of the capital owner's ownership. Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a ruling from the matn. It clarifies that when a mudarib purchases a slave from the capital owner himself, the purchase is valid but has a potential defect (shubhat al-'adam) because it is essentially a sale of the capital owner's own property to himself through the mudarib. Since murabahah is a trust-based contract, any suspicion of betrayal must be avoided. Therefore, when reporting the cost for murabahah, the mudarib must declare the lower of the two possible prices, which is half of the capital (500 dirhams). The commentary explains the reasoning: the first purchase was by the capital owner, and the second purchase is also effectively by him, as the mudarib's possession does not transfer ownership. The second sale is valid only due to necessity (to allow the mudarib to handle the asset), but it retains the semblance of being a sale of one's own property to oneself. Hence, for murabahah, the lower price is used.

Key Terms
مضارب (mudarib): The agent in a mudarabah contract who manages the capital and receives a share of the profit.
مرابحة (murabahah): A sale where the seller discloses the cost and adds a profit margin; it is a trust-based contract.
شبهة العدم (shubhat al-'adam): A semblance (doubt) that the second contract did not actually occur because it is essentially the same as the first.
أقل الثمنين (aqall al-thamanayn): The lower of the two prices (here, 500 dirhams) that the mudarib must report in a murabahah sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario described in the passage, what does the mudarib say as the cost when selling on murabahah?
A) 'It cost me one thousand dirhams'
B) 'It cost me half of the thousand (500 dirhams)'
C) 'It cost me the market value'
D) 'It cost me nothing because it belongs to the capital owner'

Key Takeaway
When a mudarib buys from the capital owner, the murabahah cost must be the lower of the two possible prices due to the doubt in the validity of the second purchase.

Daf' and Fida' for a Mudarabah Slave Who Kills
Explains fida' apportionment and conditions for daf' in mudarabah slave manslaughter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the fida' shares for a mudarabah slave who commits manslaughter and identify the conditions for daf' and fida'.

Core Idea
When a mudarabah slave kills, both owners must be present for daf'; fida' is divided by ownership shares.

The source passage explains the ruling for a jointly owned slave in mudarabah who commits accidental manslaughter. The victim's heirs may claim the slave (daf') or demand blood money (fida'). The Hanafi school provides detailed rules on who must be present for each option and how the fida' is apportioned based on ownership shares. This lesson unpacks those rules and the underlying analogy to a mortgaged slave.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Understand the base case: mudarib buys a slave for 1000 dirhams, slave is worth 2000, slave kills accidentally. Determine the ownership shares (mudarib owns 1/4, capital owner owns 3/4).
2
Determine the options for the victim's heirs
The heirs may either demand the slave (daf') or demand ransom (fida'). These are mutually exclusive choices.
3
Analyze the requirement for daf'
For daf', both the mudarib and the capital owner must be present. This is derived by analogy with a mortgaged slave (rahn), which also requires both parties.
The presence condition applies regardless of the slave's value relative to the blood money.
4
Analyze the rules for fida'
For fida', the presence of both is not required. If one is absent, the present one may pay fida' but only as a volunteer and cannot recover from the absent party.
Qadi Khan holds that the mudarib cannot act alone in either daf' or fida'.
5
Calculate fida' shares
Fida' is apportioned according to ownership shares. In the example: mudarib owns 1/4 (500/2000), so pays 1/4 of fida'; capital owner pays 3/4.
The calculation is based on the slave's value, not just the capital.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٤] قوله : ولـو شـرى...الخ ؛ يعني إنّ المضارب بالنصف لو اشترى بألف المضاربة عبداً تساوي قيمته ألفين، فقتل ذلك العبد رجلاً قتلاً خطاً، فأمر بالدفع أو الفداء، فإذا دفعا العبد إلى ولي المقتول انتهت المضاربة بهلاكِ مالها بالدفع بلا بدل، وكذا إن فديا خرج العبد عن المضاربة. يعدل ضعفه ، فقتل رجلاً خطأ ، فربعُ الفداء عليه، وباقيه على المالك) : أي إذا امتنعا عن الدفع، واختارا الفداء يعني أَرْسَ الجناية، يفديان بقدر الملك، والعبد ربعُهُ للمضارب ؛ لأنَّ رأس المال ألف، والعبد يساوي ألفين، (وإذا فديا خرج عنها، فيخدم المضارب يوماً، والمالك ثلاثة أيام) أما خروج حصة المضارب فلتقرُّرِ ملكه في العبد بالفداء، فصار كالقسمة، وأمّا خروج حصة المالك فسلامةِ الحصة منه بضمان الفداء، فربع الفداء على المضارب، وباقيه وهو ثلاثة أرباعه على المالك ؛ لأنَّ الفداء مؤنة الملك، فيتقدر بقدره، وقد كان الملك بينهما أرباعا، فكذا الفداء. [١]قوله : يعدل ضعفه ؛ إنّما قيد به لأنه لو كان قيمته ألفاً فجنايته على ربِّ المال بلا خلاف. كذا في «البناية». [٢] قوله : فقتل رجلاً خطأ ؛ اعلم أنّ العبد المشترى في المضاربة إذا جنى خطاً لا يدفع بها حتى يحضر المضارب وربُّ المال، سواء كان الأرش مثل قيمة العبد أو أقل أو أكثر ، وكذا لو كانت قيمته ألفا لا غير لا يدفع إلا بحضرتهما ؛ لأنَّ المضارب له فيه حق ملك ، حتى ليس لرب المال أن يأخذه ويمنعُهُ عن بيعه، كالمرهون إذا جنى خطأ لا يدفع إلا بحضرة الراهن والمرتهن. والحاصل أنه يشترط حضرة ربِّ المالِ والمضارب للدفع دون الفداء، إلا إذا أبي المضارب الدفع أو الفداء، وقيمته مثل رأس المال فلرب المال دفعه لتعينه، فإن كان أحدهما غائباً، وقيمة العبد ألفا درهم، ففداه الحاضر كان متطوعاً ؛ لأنه أدى دين غيره بغير أمره، وهو غير مضطر فيه، فإنّه لو أقامَ البيِّنة على الشركة لا يطالب بحصة صاحبه لا بالدفع ولا بالفداء. كذا في «النهاية». وذكر قاضي خان في «فتاواه»: إنَّ المضارب ليس له الدفع والفداء وحده ؛ لأنه ليس من أحكام المضاربة ؛ فلهذا كان إليهما.
[4] His statement: 'And if he buys...' meaning that the mudarib with half-profit, if he buys with the thousand of the mudarabah a slave worth two thousand, then that slave kills a man by manslaughter, so the matter is either payment (def') or ransom (fida'). If they pay the slave to the heir of the slain, the mudarabah ends due to loss of its capital by payment without compensation. Likewise, if they ransom, the slave leaves the mudarabah. 'It equals double' so it kills a man by mistake, so a quarter of the ransom is due from him, and the rest from the owner): i.e., if they refrain from payment and choose ransom, meaning the blood money, they ransom according to ownership. The slave's quarter belongs to the mudarib because the capital is one thousand and the slave is worth two thousand. 'And if they ransom, it leaves the mudarabah; the mudarib serves one day and the owner three days.' As for the leaving of the mudarib's share, it is due to the establishment of his ownership in the slave by the ransom, so it becomes like division. As for the leaving of the owner's share, it is for the safety of his share from being liable for the ransom. So a quarter of the ransom is on the mudarib, and the rest, i.e., three quarters, on the owner, because the ransom is an expense of ownership, so it is proportioned accordingly. [1] His statement: 'it equals double' – he only restricted it because if its value were one thousand, then its crime is on the owner without disagreement. Thus in al-Binaya. [2] His statement: 'then it kills a man by mistake' – know that when a slave purchased in mudarabah commits manslaughter, he is not to be handed over until the mudarib and the capital owner are present, whether the blood money is equal to the slave's value, or less, or more. Likewise, if its value is only one thousand, it is not handed over except in their presence, because the mudarib has a right of ownership in it, so much so that the owner cannot take it and prevent him from selling it, like a mortgaged slave when it commits manslaughter, it is not handed over except in the presence of the mortgagor and mortgagee. The conclusion is that the presence of the capital owner and the mudarib is required for handing over, but not for ransom, unless if the mudarib refuses to hand over or ransom, and its value is like the capital, then the owner may hand it over because it is his specific right. If one of them is absent, and the slave's value is two thousand dirhams, and the present one ransoms, he is a volunteer, because he paid the debt of another without his permission, and he is not compelled therein. For if he establishes proof of partnership, he cannot claim his partner's share either for handing over or for ransom. Thus in al-Nihaya. And Qadi Khan mentioned in his Fatawa: 'The mudarib does not have the right to hand over or ransom alone, because that is not among the rulings of mudarabah; therefore, it is for the two of them.'
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage discusses a case where the mudarib buys a slave for 1000 dirhams, and the slave is worth 2000. The slave commits accidental manslaughter. The heirs of the victim have a choice: demand the slave (def') or demand blood money (fida'). If they take the slave, the mudarabah ends (the capital is lost). If they choose fida', the mudarib and capital owner pay according to their shares: one-fourth (500) by the mudarib and three-fourths (1500) by the capital owner. The commentary explains that this is because the mudarib owns one-fourth of the slave (his profit share is half of the excess value; the excess over capital is 1000, so his share is 500, which is one-fourth of the total value 2000). The fida' is an expense of ownership, so it is divided by shares. The passage also states that when a slave commits manslaughter, both the mudarib and capital owner must be present for the def', but not necessarily for the fida'. If one is absent, the present one can pay fida' but only as a volunteer and cannot recover from the absent one. This is from al-Nihaya. Qadi Khan adds that the mudarib cannot act alone in def' or fida' because it is not within his authority.

Key Terms
دفع (daf'): Handing over the slave to the victim's heirs as compensation (instead of paying blood money).
فداء (fida'): Ransom paid to free the slave from liability; blood money paid by the owners to retain ownership.
أرش (arsh): Blood money or compensation for injury; here synonymous with fida'.
رهن (rahn): Mortgage; used as analogy for the mudarabah slave's joint ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Half (1000 dirhams)
B) One-fourth (500 dirhams)
C) One-third (approximately 666 dirhams)
D) Nothing; the capital owner pays all

Key Takeaway
The fida' for a mudarabah slave who kills is divided by ownership shares, and daf' requires both parties' presence, while fida' does not.

Division of Ransom for a Mudarabah Slave's Manslaughter
Commentary on division of ransom for a mudarabah slave's manslaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that ransom for a mudarabah slave's manslaughter is divided according to ownership shares, and distinguish the conditions for surrender versus ransom.

Core Idea
Ransom follows ownership: the cost of retaining a jointly-owned slave is proportional to each owner's share.

This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah clarifies a specific scenario in mudarabah: a slave purchased with partnership capital commits manslaughter. The owners have two options: surrender the slave (daf') or pay ransom (fida'). The critical point is how the ransom is divided if they choose to pay. The Hanafi school derives the rule from the principle that expenses of ownership are borne in proportion to one's share, analogized to pawned property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Two Options
When a mudarabah slave commits manslaughter, the owners may either surrender the slave to the victim's heirs or pay a ransom. Recognize that the ruling focuses on the ransom scenario.
The passage assumes both parties choose ransom over surrender unless specified otherwise.
2
Determine Ownership Shares in the Slave
Calculate the ownership ratio: if capital (ra's al-mal) is 1000 and the slave's value is 2000, the mudarib's share is 1/4 (his profit/ownership increment) and the capital owner's share is 3/4. This ratio is the basis for dividing the ransom.
Ownership shares are determined by the actual value relative to the capital invested.
3
Apply the Principle: Ransom is an Expense of Ownership
The commentary states that 'al-fida' mu'nat al-milk' – ransom is an expense of ownership. Therefore, each owner must pay in proportion to his ownership share. The mudarib pays 1/4 of the ransom, the capital owner pays 3/4.
This contrasts with profit sharing, which is based on agreement; here the expense is necessarily proportional to actual ownership.
4
Distinguish Conditions for Surrender vs. Ransom
Surrender (daf') requires the presence of both the mudarib and capital owner, analogous to a pawned slave. Ransom (fida') does not require both present; but if one party is absent and the other ransoms alone, he is a volunteer and cannot recover from the absent partner. Also, if the mudarib refuses and the slave's value equals the capital, the owner may surrender alone.
This distinction is important for understanding who bears liability and when unilateral action is permitted.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the ruling on a slave purchased with mudarabah capital who commits manslaughter. The matn states the slave's value is double the capital, so ownership is divided: one-quarter to the mudarib (since capital is 1000, slave value 2000) and three-quarters to the capital owner. If both parties choose to pay ransom instead of surrendering the slave, they pay proportionally to their ownership: the mudarib pays one quarter of the ransom, the owner pays three quarters. The reasoning is that ransom is a cost of ownership, so it follows ownership shares. After ransom, the slave is freed from mudarabah because it becomes like a division. The commentary adds important conditions: surrender of the slave for the crime requires presence of both parties, but ransom does not, except if the mudarib refuses and the slave's value equals the capital, then the owner can surrender alone. If one party is absent and the other ransoms, they are considered a volunteer and cannot recover from the absent partner. Qadi Khan's fatwa confirms that the mudarib alone cannot surrender or ransom because these are not part of the mudarabah contract. The passage also notes that if the judge decrees division of the ransom, it implies division of the slave, ending the mudarabah.

Key Terms
الفداء (al-fida'): The ransom paid to avoid surrendering the slave for his crime; it is a monetary compensation.
المضاربة (al-mudarabah): A contract of commenda where one party provides capital and the other provides labor, with profit sharing as agreed.
الدفع (al-daf'): Surrendering the slave to the victim's heirs in compensation for manslaughter.
مؤنة الملك (mu'nat al-milk): Expense of ownership; the costs incident to owning property.

Mudarib's Repeated Recourse vs. Agent's One-Time Recourse
Ruling on mudarib's recourse when capital lost repeatedly before paying slave's price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the mudarib's repeated recourse from the agent's limited recourse by applying the Hanafi concepts of amana (trust) and istifa' (satisfaction).

Core Idea
Mudarib's capital is amana; agent's receipt is istifa'. Hence, capital owner bears repeated loss for mudarib, but only once for agent.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains a crucial distinction in Hanafi mu'amalat: when capital is lost before paying the seller, the mudarib can request replacement repeatedly, whereas an agent can only do so once. The key lies in how each custody is legally classified — trust versus guarantee. Understanding this difference is essential for correctly applying mudarabah contracts in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for mudarib
The mudarib recourses against the capital owner every time the capital is lost before payment, ad infinitum. The entire capital paid becomes the new capital.
This is the established Hanafi position (zahir al-riwayah).
2
Contrast with the agent (wakil)
An agent who receives the price after purchase cannot recourse if lost. The receipt is istifa' (satisfaction of a debt), converting it into a guarantee (daman).
The agent owes the principal the price, so receipt satisfies that debt.
3
Determine the legal basis
Mudarabah is based on trust; the mudarib's hand is a trust hand (yad amana). Istifa' only occurs with guaranteed possession, which contradicts mudarabah.
Key phrase: 'المضاربة تنافيه' (mudarabah is inconsistent with guarantee).
4
Recognize the exception for agents
If the agent receives the price before purchase, that receipt is a trust (amana). If lost then, the agent can recourse because no debt existed yet.
Pre-purchase receipt cannot be istifa' as no obligation is owed.
5
Apply to termination of mudarabah
The passage briefly notes that if the capital is lost after purchase, it may lead to division of assets and end of mudarabah, unlike loss of expenses.
This connects to an earlier ruling about the slave's manslaughter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اشترى عبداً بألفها، وهلك الألف قبل نقدِه ، دفع رب المال ثمنه، ثم وثمّ [١] قوله : يتضمن انقسام العبد ؛ لأنَّ الخطاب بالفداء يوجب سلامة المفــدي للفادي، ولا سلامة إلا بالقسمة، والمضاربة تنتهي بالقسمة، بخلاف ما إذا ضـاع الإنفاق، حيث لا تنتهي المضاربة هناك، بل تثبت على ما كانت ؛ لأنَّ جميع الثمن في هذه الصورة يكون على المضارب، وإن كان له حق الرجوع على ربِّ المال فلا حاجةً ذلك. إلى القسمة ؛ لعدم أمر تقتضي [٢] قوله : ولو اشترى...الخ ؛ يعني إذا كان مع المضارب ألف درهم فاشترى به عبداً، وضاع الثمن قبل النقدِ رجع على ربِّ المال، فإذا دفع إليه ثانياً ثم هلك قبل النقدِ أيضاً رجع عليه أيضاً، وهكذا يرجعُ عليه كلّما هلك إلى ما لا يتناهى، ويكون رأس المال جميع ما دفع إليه رب المال، بخلاف الوكيل، حيث لا يرجع عند هلاكِ الثمن بعد الشراء إلا مرة واحدة. والفرق أنَّ المال في يد المضارب أمانة لا يمكن حمله على الاستيفاء ؛ لأن الاستيفاء لا يكون إلا بقبض مضمون، والمضاربة تنافيه على ما بينا سابقاً، فكل ما قبض يكون أمانة ، وإذا هلك كان الهالك على ربِّ المال. وقبض الوكيل بعد الشراء استيفاء ؛ لأنه وجب له على الموكل مثل ما وجب عليه للبائع، فإذا قبضه صارَ مستوفياً لذلك، فصار مضموناً عليه، فإذا هلك ليس له أن يرجع به على الموكل ؛ لأنَّ المستوفى لم يبق له حقٌّ بعد الاستيفاء، ولم يوجد ما يمنعُ من جعله مستوفياً لحقه مضموناً عليه؛ لأنَّ الوكالة لا تنافى الضمان. ألا ترى أن الغاصب إذا توكّل ببيع المغصوب جاز، وهو مضمون عليه، فلا حاجة إلى جعل ما قبضه بعد الشراء أمانة، حتى لو لم يقع استيفاء بأن دفع إليه الثمن قبل الشراء، ثم اشترى به، ثم هلك قبل النقد، رجع به على الموكل ؛ لوقوع الأول أمانة ؛ لأنه لا يمكن جعله مستوفياً بقبضه قبل الشراء ؛ لأنه لم يجب له عليه شيء، حتى يصير مستوفياً بالقبض، فيكون أمانة ، فإذا هلك رجع عليه فيكون مضموناً عليه، ثمّ إذا هلك لا يرجع لما ذكرنا.
And if he buys a slave with one thousand, and the one thousand perishes before paying it, the capital owner pays its price, then again. [1] His saying: it entails division of the slave; because the address regarding ransom necessitates the safety of the ransomed for the ransomer, and there is no safety except through division, and mudarabah ends with division. Unlike when the expenditure is lost, where mudarabah does not end there, rather it remains as it was, because the entire price in this case becomes on the mudarib, even though he has the right to recourse against the capital owner, so there is no need for division because there is no matter that requires it. [2] His saying: And if he buys...etc.; meaning if the mudarib has one thousand dirhams and buys a slave with it, and the price is lost before payment, he recourses against the capital owner. If he pays him again and then it is lost before payment again, he recourses again, and so on, he recourses every time it is lost ad infinitum, and the capital becomes all that the capital owner has paid to him. Unlike an agent, who does not recourse when the price is lost after purchase except once. The difference is that the money in the hand of the mudarib is an amana (trust) and cannot be construed as istifa' (receipt in satisfaction) because istifa' only occurs through guaranteed possession, and mudarabah is inconsistent with that, as we explained earlier. So everything he receives is a trust, and if it perishes, the loss is on the capital owner. The agent's receipt after purchase is istifa' because he owes the principal something like what he owes the seller. So when he receives it, he becomes having satisfied that, so it becomes guaranteed on him. So if it perishes, he cannot recourse with it against the principal, because one who has satisfied has no remaining right after satisfaction, and there is nothing to prevent him from being considered one who satisfied his right and thereby guaranteed, because agency does not contradict guarantee. Do you not see that if a usurper is appointed as agent to sell the usurped item, it is permissible and it is guaranteed on him? So there is no need to make what he receives after purchase a trust. Even if istifa' does not occur, as when the price is paid to him before purchase, then he buys with it, then it perishes before payment, he recourses with it against the principal, because the first receipt was a trust, since it cannot be considered istifa' by receipt before purchase because nothing is owed to him at that time, so it is a trust. If it perishes, he recourses, then it becomes guaranteed on him. Then if it perishes again, he does not recourse for the reason mentioned.
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the rule when a mudarib uses capital to buy a slave but the capital is lost before paying the seller. The matn states that the capital owner pays the price again, and if lost again, pays again repeatedly. The commentary clarifies that the mudarib can recourse against the capital owner every time the capital is lost, because the capital in his hand is an amana (trust), so any loss is borne by the capital owner. This is unlike a regular agent (wakil) who, after purchasing, receives the price from the principal as istifa' (satisfaction of a debt owed to him), making it guaranteed on the agent. If the agent loses it, he cannot recourse. The reason is that the mudarib's receipts are all amana because mudarabah is incompatible with guarantee. The agent, after purchase, has a claim against the principal for the price, so when he receives it, it satisfies his claim, becoming guaranteed. A key exception: if the agent receives the price before purchase, then that receipt is a trust, so if lost, the agent can recourse. The commentary also connects back to the earlier ruling about the slave's manslaughter, noting that the division of ransom implies division of the slave, ending mudarabah, unlike the case of lost expenses where the mudarabah continues.

Key Terms
الأمانة (al-amanah): Property held in trust, where the holder is not liable for loss unless negligent.
الاستيفاء (al-istifa'): Receipt of a debt or owed item in satisfaction of a claim, making the receiver liable.
الوكيل (al-wakil): An agent appointed to perform a legal act on behalf of another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the mudarib's receipt is treated as an amana, not an istifa'
C) Because the capital owner is richer
D) Because the mudarib is not required to pay the seller

Key Takeaway
The mudarib's possession remains an amana unless converted by istifa', so the capital owner repeatedly bears the loss of capital lost before payment.

The Mudarib's Multiple Reimbursement Right vs the Wakil's Single Recourse
Ruling on mudarib's right to multiple reimbursements when capital lost before payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the mudarib's and wakil's rights to reimbursement when the price is lost before payment and explain the legal basis (amana vs istifa) for the difference.

Core Idea
The mudarib's possession is amana, so loss is on the owner; the wakil's possession is istifa, so he bears further loss.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah contrasts two similar commercial agents: the mudarib (working partner) and the wakil (purchase agent). Although both may purchase goods with the principal's money and both may lose the money before paying the seller, their rights to seek replacement money differ fundamentally. The key lies in the nature of their possession: trust (amana) versus satisfaction of a debt (istifa). Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly allocating risk in mudarabah and agency contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling for the mudarib
Consider a mudarib who receives capital, buys an item, but loses the money before paying the seller. According to the passage, the rabb al-mal must pay again and again for each loss, and all such payments become part of the capital.
The ruling is that the mudarib can seek reimbursement indefinitely.
2
Identify the scenario and ruling for the wakil
Now consider a wakil (purchase agent) in the same situation: he buys an item but loses the price after the purchase. Unlike the mudarib, he can only seek reimbursement once; if he loses the money again, he cannot ask for another payment.
The wakil's right to recourse is limited to one time.
3
Locate the illa (effective cause) for the difference
The passage explains that the difference stems from the nature of possession in each case. The mudarib holds the capital as an amana (trust), which is not guaranteed. The wakil, after purchase, holds the price as istifa (satisfaction of a debt), which is a guaranteed (daman) possession. This difference determines whether the loss falls on the principal or the agent.
The illa is the type of possession: amana vs. istifa (daman).
4
Understand the underlying principles
Delve into why amana cannot be istifa: istifa requires a guaranteed possession (qabd madmun), but mudarabah is built on trust, so the mudarib's possession is never guaranteed. In contrast, agency (wakalah) is compatible with guarantee, so the wakil's taking becomes istifa. This principle is reinforced by the example of a usurper (ghasib) acting as agent, which is permissible despite guarantee.
The key principle: mudarabah contradicts daman, agency does not.
5
Apply the ruling to variants
Consider a variant: if the wakil receives the price before purchase instead of after, his possession is amana (not istifa), so he can seek reimbursement like the mudarib. Conversely, if the mudarib receives money after a transaction (e.g., from profit), the ruling may differ. This step tests your ability to extend the principle.
The timing of receipt (before/after purchase) affects the nature of possession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المضاربة المضارب الذي يضارب
ولو اشترى عبداً بألفها، وهلك الألف قبل نقدِه ، دفع رب المال ثمنه، ثم وثمّ إنما يخرج العبد عن المضارية ؛ لأن قضاء القاضي بانقسام الفداء يتضمن انقسام العبد، والمضاربة تنتهي بالقسمة. (ولو اشترى عبداً بألفها ، وهلك الألف قبل نقدِه ، دفع رب المال ثمنه ، ثم وثم) [١] قوله : يتضمن انقسام العبد ؛ لأنَّ الخطاب بالفداء يوجب سلامة المفــدي للفادي، ولا سلامة إلا بالقسمة، والمضاربة تنتهي بالقسمة، بخلاف ما إذا ضـاع الإنفاق، حيث لا تنتهي المضاربة هناك، بل تثبت على ما كانت ؛ لأنَّ جميع الثمن في هذه الصورة يكون على المضارب، وإن كان له حق الرجوع على ربِّ المال فلا حاجةً ذلك. إلى القسمة ؛ لعدم أمر تقتضي [٢] قوله : ولو اشترى...الخ ؛ يعني إذا كان مع المضارب ألف درهم فاشترى به عبداً، وضاع الثمن قبل النقدِ رجع على ربِّ المال، فإذا دفع إليه ثانياً ثم هلك قبل النقدِ أيضاً رجع عليه أيضاً، وهكذا يرجعُ عليه كلّما هلك إلى ما لا يتناهى، ويكون رأس المال جميع ما دفع إليه رب المال، بخلاف الوكيل، حيث لا يرجع عند هلاكِ الثمن بعد الشراء إلا مرة واحدة. والفرق أنَّ المال في يد المضارب أمانة لا يمكن حمله على الاستيفاء ؛ لأن الاستيفاء لا يكون إلا بقبض مضمون، والمضاربة تنافيه على ما بينا سابقاً، فكل ما قبض يكون أمانة ، وإذا هلك كان الهالك على ربِّ المال.
وقبض الوكيل بعد الشراء استيفاء ؛ لأنه وجب له على الموكل مثل ما وجب عليه للبائع، فإذا قبضه صارَ مستوفياً لذلك، فصار مضموناً عليه، فإذا هلك ليس له أن يرجع به على الموكل ؛ لأنَّ المستوفى لم يبق له حقٌّ بعد الاستيفاء، ولم يوجد ما يمنعُ من جعله مستوفياً لحقه مضموناً عليه؛ لأنَّ الوكالة لا تنافى الضمان.
ألا ترى أن الغاصب إذا توكّل ببيع المغصوب جاز، وهو مضمون عليه، فلا حاجة إلى جعل ما قبضه بعد الشراء أمانة، حتى لو لم يقع استيفاء بأن دفع إليه الثمن قبل الشراء، ثم اشترى به، ثم هلك قبل النقد، رجع به على الموكل ؛ لوقوع الأول أمانة ؛ لأنه لا يمكن جعله مستوفياً بقبضه قبل الشراء ؛ لأنه لم يجب له عليه شيء، حتى يصير مستوفياً بالقبض، فيكون أمانة ، فإذا هلك رجع عليه فيكون مضموناً عليه، ثمّ إذا هلك لا يرجع لما ذكرنا.
وجميع ما دفع رأس ماله.
أي إذا دَفَعَ رَبُّ المالِ ثمنه ، وهَلَكَ في يد المضارب قبل أن يؤدِّيه إلى البائعِ يَدْفَعُ المال إلى المضارب ثمنه مرَّةً أخرى ، وهكذا إن هَلَكَ في يده، (وجميع ما دُفِعَ رأسُ ماله.
بخلاف ما إذا لم يدفع إليه الثمن إلا بعد الشراء ، حيث لا يرجع أصلاً، والمعنى ما بيناه ؛ ولأن ما قبضه الوكيل لو لم يحمل على الاستيفاء لزم منه تضييع المال على الموكل ؛ لأنَّ المأخوذ منه ثانياً يضيع. وفي المضاربة لا يضيع ؛ لأنه ملحق برأس المال، ويستوفيه من الربح، ولو لم يرجع عليه لتضرر المضارب، فيرجع عليه دفعاً للضَّررِ . عنه ؛ ولأنَّ الوكيل انتهت وكالته بالشراء مرة وانعزل فلا يرجعُ بعد الانعزال، بخلاف المضارب، فإنّه لم ينعزل بالتصرف، بل لا ينعزل بالعزل في بعض الصور، فيرجع عليه ما دام متصرفاً له. كذا في
«التبيين"
(1)
11 ] قوله : يدفع رب المالِ إلى المضارب ثمنه مرة أخرى ؛ لأنَّ الشراء لا يبطل بهلاكِ الثمن، فيبقى موجباً دين الثمن عليه، وهو عامل لرب المال فيستوجب عليه مثل ما وجـب عـلـيـه مـن الـديـن في العمل، واستيفاء ذلك لا يقع بقبض هذه الألوف ؛ لأنَّ جميعها يصير رأس مال المضاربة.
وقبض رأس المال قبض ،أمانة، واستيفاء الدين إنّما يكون بقبض مضمون ، وقبض الأمانة لا ينوب عن القبض المضمون ؛ فلذا يرجع إليه مرة بعد أخرى إلى أن يسقط عنه الثمن، بوصول الثمن إلى البائع. كذا في «الكفاية»(٢).
Book of Mudarabah: The mudarib who enters into mudarabah. If he bought a slave for one thousand (dirhams) and the thousand was lost before paying it, the capital owner pays its price, then again and again. The slave is removed from the mudarabah only because the judge's ruling on dividing the ransom implies division of the slave, and the mudarabah ends with division. (If he bought a slave for one thousand, and the thousand was lost before paying it, the capital owner pays its price, then and again.) [1] He said: It implies division of the slave because the address regarding ransom necessitates the safety of the ransomed for the ransomer, and safety is only through division, and mudarabah ends with division. Unlike when the expenditure is lost, where mudarabah does not end, but remains as it was, because all of the price in this case is on the mudarib, even if he has the right to recourse against the capital owner, there is no need for division due to lack of something necessitating [2] He said: 'And if he bought...' etc.; meaning, if the mudarib had one thousand dirhams and bought a slave with it, and the price was lost before payment, he has recourse against the capital owner. If he paid him a second time and then it was lost before payment as well, he has recourse again, and so on, he has recourse every time it is lost indefinitely, and the capital becomes all that the capital owner paid. Unlike the wakil, who does not have recourse when the price is lost after purchase except once. The difference is that the money in the mudarib's hand is a trust (amana) and cannot be interpreted as satisfaction (istifa) because satisfaction is only by guaranteed (daman) possession, and mudarabah contradicts that as we explained earlier. So everything he takes is a trust, and if it is lost, the loss is on the capital owner. The wakil's possession after purchase is satisfaction because the same amount owed to the seller becomes owed to him by the principal. So when he takes it, he becomes the recipient of that satisfaction, and it becomes guaranteed (daman) upon him. So if it is lost, he cannot have recourse to the principal because the recipient has no further right after satisfaction, and there is nothing preventing him from being considered a recipient of his right with guarantee because agency (wakalah) does not contradict guarantee. Do you not see that if a usurper (ghasib) is appointed as agent to sell the usurped property, it is permissible, and it is guaranteed upon him. So there is no need to make what he takes after purchase a trust. So if satisfaction did not occur, such as if he gave him the price before purchase, then he bought with it, then it was lost before payment, he has recourse against the principal because the first taking was a trust, because it cannot be made satisfaction by taking before purchase, since nothing was owed to him yet to make him a recipient by taking. So it is a trust, and if it is lost, he has recourse, and then if it is lost again, he does not have recourse for what we mentioned. And all that was paid is his capital. That is, if the capital owner pays its price, and it is lost in the mudarib's hand before he gives it to the seller, he pays the money to the mudarib as its price another time, and so on if it is lost in his hand, (and all that is paid is his capital. Unlike if he did not pay him the price except after purchase, where he does not have recourse at all. The meaning is what we explained. And because if the wakil's taking were not interpreted as satisfaction, it would lead to wasting the principal's money because the second taking would be lost. In mudarabah, it is not lost because it is added to the capital and he recovers it from the profit. And if he did not have recourse, the mudarib would be harmed, so he has recourse to prevent harm. And because the wakil's agency ends with the purchase once and he is dismissed, so he does not have recourse after dismissal. Unlike the mudarib, who is not dismissed by this action; rather he is not dismissed by dismissal in some cases, so he has recourse as long as he is acting. This is in Al-Tabyin. (1) [11] He said: The capital owner pays the mudarib its price another time because the purchase is not invalidated by the loss of the price; rather it remains obligating the debt of the price upon him, and he is an agent for the capital owner, so he becomes entitled to the same as what became owed to him from the debt in the work. And satisfaction of that does not occur by taking these thousands because all of it becomes the capital of mudarabah. Taking the capital is a trust-taking, and satisfaction of a debt is only by guaranteed taking, and trust-taking does not substitute for guaranteed taking. Therefore he has recourse again and again until the price is discharged from him by reaching the seller. This is in Al-Kifayah. (2)
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter on Mudarabah from the commentary 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah. It addresses the scenario where a mudarib purchases an item with the capital but loses the money before paying the seller. The ruling is that the rabb al-mal must pay repeatedly for each loss, and all such payments become part of the capital. This is contrasted with the case of a wakil (purchase agent) who can only seek reimbursement once if the money is lost after purchase. The key reasoning is the nature of possession: the mudarib holds the capital as an amana (trust), which does not constitute istifa (satisfaction of a debt) because istifa requires a daman (guaranteed) possession. Since the mudarib's possession is never guaranteed, each loss is ultimately the rabb al-mal's responsibility. In contrast, the wakil's possession after purchase is istifa because he becomes entitled to the same sum from the principal; thus once he takes it, his debt is satisfied and he cannot claim again. The text further supports this with an analogy: if a usurper (ghasib) is appointed as agent, his possession is guaranteed, showing that agency and guarantee are compatible. The passage also notes that the mudarib remains in his role and can seek reimbursement repeatedly, unlike the wakil whose agency terminates upon purchase.

Key Terms
المضارب (al-mudarib): The working partner in a mudarabah contract who receives capital and manages trade.
الوكيل (al-wakil): An agent appointed to purchase; his possession after purchase is istifa (satisfaction of debt).
الأمانة (al-amana): Trust property; the mudarib's possession is amana, so loss is on the owner.
الاستيفاء (al-istifa): Satisfaction of a debt by taking possession; wakil's taking is istifa because the same sum is owed to him.
القبض المضمون (al-qabd al-madmun): Guaranteed possession, where the holder is liable for loss; applies to wakil after purchase.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the mudarib receive multiple reimbursements for lost capital while the wakil only receives one?
A) Because the mudarib is always entitled to more profit
B) Because the mudarib's possession is amana, while the wakil's possession after purchase is istifa
C) Because the mudarib's contract never ends
D) Because the wakil is negligent

Key Takeaway
The distinguishing factor between mudarib and wakil in reimbursement rights is the nature of possession: amana for mudarib (so multiple recourse) and istifa for wakil (single recourse).

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate

Mudarib's Loss of Price Money and Reimbursement
Ruling on repeated payment when mudarib loses price money

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires the capital provider to repeatedly reimburse the mudarib when price money is lost, and distinguish this ruling from the case of an ordinary agent.

Core Idea
The mudarib's loss of price money does not invalidate the purchase; the capital provider must pay again to fulfill the debt, preventing harm to the mudarib.

In a mudarabah, the mudarib buys goods on behalf of the capital provider. If the price money is lost before reaching the seller, who bears the cost? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that the capital provider must reimburse the mudarib repeatedly, unlike an ordinary agent. The reasoning balances legal principles of debt, trust, and avoidance of harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
State that the mudarib receives the price money from the capital provider but loses it before paying the seller. The ruling is that the capital provider must pay the price again, and repeatedly if lost again.
This applies only if the money is lost after receipt but before delivery to the seller.
2
Understand the proof
The purchase contract remains valid despite the loss; the price becomes a debt on the mudarib. Reimbursement is wajib to remove harm (darar) from the mudarib, based on the principle of istihsan.
The proof relies on the hadith 'La darar wa la dirar' as a basis for preventing harm.
3
Compare with a wakil
An ordinary agent (wakil) who loses price money after purchase does not get reimbursed because his agency ends with the purchase, and giving him money again would waste the principal's capital. The mudarib differs because he is not dismissed by the transaction.
This contrast clarifies why the ruling is specific to mudarabah.
4
Analyze the illa (effective cause)
In mudarabah, the money received by the mudarib becomes part of the capital and can be recovered from profit; thus no waste occurs. The mudarib continues as an agent, so reimbursement is justified to prevent harm.
The illa is khafiyyah (hidden) and is identified through tanqih al-manat.
5
Note the legal method
Qiyas would treat the mudarib like a wakil and deny reimbursement, but istihsan overrides qiyas to avoid hardship. This is a classic example of Hanafi istihsan based on public benefit and harm prevention.
The authority is from later Hanafi works (Tabyin, Kifayah), representing the fatwa position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجميع ما دفع رأس ماله. أي إذا دفع رب المال ثمنه، وهلك في يد المضارب قبل أن يؤديه إلى البائع يدفع المال إلى المضارب ثمنه مرة أخرى، وهكذا إن هلك في يده. [1] بخلاف ما إذا لم يدفع إليه الثمن إلا بعد الشراء، حيث لا يرجع أصلاً، والمعنى ما بيناه؛ ولأن ما قبضه الوكيل لو لم يحمل على الاستيفاء لزم منه تضييع المال على الموكل؛ لأن المأخوذ منه ثانياً يضيع. وفي المضاربة لا يضيع؛ لأنه ملحق برأس المال، ويستوفيه من الربح، ولو لم يرجع عليه لتضرر المضارب، فيرجع عليه دفعاً للضرر. عنه؛ ولأن الوكيل انتهت وكالته بالشراء مرة وانعزل فلا يرجع بعد الانعزال، بخلاف المضارب، فإنه لم ينعزل بالتصرف، بل لا ينعزل بالعزل في بعض الصور، فيرجع عليه ما دام متصرفاً له. كذا في "التبيين" (1) [1] قوله: يدفع رب المال إلى المضارب ثمنه مرة أخرى؛ لأن الشراء لا يبطل بهلاك الثمن، فيبقى موجباً دين الثمن عليه، وهو عامل لرب المال فيستوجب عليه مثل ما وجب عليه من الدين في العمل، واستيفاء ذلك لا يقع بقبض هذه الألوف؛ لأن جميعها يصير رأس مال المضاربة. وقبض رأس المال قبض أمانة، واستيفاء الدين إنما يكون بقبض مضمون، وقبض الأمانة لا ينوب عن القبض المضمون؛ فلذا يرجع إليه مرة بعد أخرى إلى أن يسقط عنه الثمن، بوصول الثمن إلى البائع. كذا في "الكفاية"(2).
And all that is paid as capital. That is, if the owner of capital pays the price, and it is lost in the hand of the mudarib before he delivers it to the seller, the owner of capital pays the price to the mudarib again, and likewise if it is lost in his hand. Unlike the case where he does not pay the price except after the purchase, where he does not recourse at all. The meaning is what we have explained; and because what the agent (wakil) receives, if it were not interpreted as collection, would lead to waste of the principal's money, because the second amount taken would be wasted. In mudarabah it is not wasted because it is annexed to the capital and he recovers it from the profit. If he did not recourse against him, the mudarib would be harmed, so he recourses against him to remove harm. Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling regarding the mudarib (the agent in a profit-sharing partnership) who loses the price money given to him by the capital provider before he pays the seller. The ruling is that the capital provider must give the mudarib the price again, and if lost again, again, until it reaches the seller. This is because the purchase contract is valid and the price remains a debt on the mudarib, and he acts for the capital provider. The distinction is made with a wakil (ordinary agent): if a wakil loses the price, he does not get reimbursed because his agency ends after purchase, and giving him the money again would waste the principal's money. In mudarabah, the money is annexed to capital and recovered from profit, so no waste. The harm to the mudarib is prevented by reimbursement. The commentator elaborates that the taking of capital is as an amanah (trust), while debt satisfaction requires a dhaman (guaranteed) taking, so trust taking doesn't suffice, necessitating repeated payment.

Key Terms
مضارب (mudarib): The agent who manages the capital in a mudarabah (profit-sharing partnership).
رب المال (rabb al-mal): The owner of the capital who provides funds in a mudarabah.
ثمن (thaman): The price of goods purchased by the mudarib on behalf of the capital provider.
رأس المال (ra's al-mal): The capital sum invested in the mudarabah.
وكيل (wakil): An ordinary agent appointed for a specific task, whose agency ends upon completion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the mudarib is a guarantor of the capital.
B) Because the purchase remains valid and the price is a debt, and the money is recoverable from profit.
C) Because the capital provider is always responsible for losses.
D) Because the mudarib can sue the seller.

Key Takeaway
The capital provider must repeatedly reimburse the mudarib for lost price money to fulfill the debt and prevent harm, based on istihsan overriding qiyas with an ordinary agent.

Dispute Between Mudarib and Capital Owner: Whose Statement is Accepted?
Intra-Hanafi dispute and rules for mudarabah disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mufta bihi Hanafi rule for resolving disputes between mudarib and capital owner and distinguish the views of Zufar and early Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
The mudarib is believed about capital received; the owner about profit share and transaction nature.

When a mudarib and capital owner disagree about the amount of capital given and profit earned, who is believed? The Hanafi school, after some internal debate, settled on believing the mudarib about the amount received. This passage from the sharh explains the reasoning and also covers disputes about the legal nature of the transaction and when both parties bring evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute scenario
Notice the specific claim: mudarib says he received 1000 as capital and made 1000 profit; owner says he gave 2000 total. This creates a dispute over the amount of capital received.
The dispute is not merely about profit but about the quantity of capital handed over.
2
State the Hanafi mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the mudarib is believed with his oath. The reasoning: the dispute is over the amount received, and the receiver is more knowledgeable.
This applies whether the mudarib is an amin (trustee) or dhamin (guarantor).
3
Contrast with Zufar's view
Zufar and the first opinion of Abu Hanifa held that the owner is believed because he denies the mudarib's profit claim, and the denier is generally believed.
The text labels this as the first view, implying it was later abandoned.
4
Apply to other sub-disputes
If the dispute is about the legal nature (loan, deposit, goods), the owner is believed. If both bring evidence, the owner's evidence prevails on capital amount, the mudarib's on profit share.
Profit share is based on the owner's stipulation, so his evidence is preferred there.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الاختلاف
وصدق مضارب قال: معي ألف دفعته إليّ، وألف ربحت، لا مالك قال: الكل دفعته. وعند زفر الله وهو القول الأول لأبي حنيفة له القول لرب المال؛ لأنه ينكر دعوى المضارب الربح، ولنا: أن الاختلاف في مقدار المقبوض، فالقول للقابض مع اليمين.
[بضاعة] ولو قال من معه ألف: هو مضاربة زيد، وقد ربح صدق زيد إن قال:
[1] قوله: وصدق...الخ؛ يعني إذا كان مع المضارب ألفان، فقال المضارب لرب المال: دفعت إلي ألفاً وربحت ألفاً، وقال المالك: لا؛ بل دفعت إليك الألفين، فالقول قول المضارب.
(2) قوله: لأنه...الخ؛ يعني لأن المضارب يدعي عليه الشركة في الربح، ورب المال ينكره، والقول يكون للمنكر. [3] قوله: ولنا...الخ؛ يعني إن الاختلاف بينهما حقيقة في مقدار المقبوض، وفي مثل هذا الاختلاف يكون القول قول القابض، سواءً كان ضميناً كالغاصب، أو أميناً كالمودع؛ لكون القابض أعرف.
بخلاف ما إذا وقع الاختلاف في صفة المقبوض من كونه قرضاً أو وديعة أو بضاعة، فالقول فيه قول رب المال، ولو قال رب المال: رأس المال ألفان، وشرطت لك ثلث الربح، قال المضارب: رأس المال ألف، وشرطت لي نصف الربح، فالقول يكون لرب المال في الربح، وللمضارب في القدر؛ لأن الربح يستحق بالشرط، وهو مستفاد من جهة رب المال.
وأيهما أقام البينة تقبل بينته كاسمها، وإن أقاما البينة في هذه الصورة كانت بينة رب المال أولى في مقدار رأس المال، وبينة المضارب أولى في مقدار الربح؛ لأنها أكثر إثباتا.
[4] قوله: ولو قال...الخ؛ يعني ولو قال من معه ألف: قد ربح فيها هي مضاربة
Chapter on Dispute
And the mudarib is believed who says: I have one thousand that you paid to me, and one thousand profit, not the owner who says: I paid all. According to Zufar (may Allah have mercy on him) and it is the first opinion of Abu Hanifa, the owner's statement is given weight because he denies the mudarib's claim of profit. Our position: the dispute is over the amount received, so the statement of the receiver is accepted with his oath.
[In the case of a bida'ah (goods)] And if someone who has one thousand says: It is a mudarabah of Zaid, and he has made profit, Zaid is believed if he says:
[1] His saying: And the mudarib is believed...etc.; meaning if the mudarib has two thousand, and he says to the owner: You paid me one thousand and I made one thousand profit, and the owner says: No, I paid you two thousand, then the mudarib's statement is accepted.
(2) His saying: Because...etc.; meaning because the mudarib claims partnership in profit, and the owner denies it, and the statement is given to the denier. [3] His saying: Our position...etc.; meaning the dispute between them is really over the amount received, and in such a dispute the statement of the receiver is accepted, whether he is a guarantor like a usurper or a trustee like a depositary; because the receiver is more knowledgeable.
Unlike when the dispute is over the description of what is received, whether it is a loan, deposit, or goods, then the statement is given to the owner. And if the owner says: The capital is two thousand and I stipulated for you one third of the profit, and the mudarib says: The capital is one thousand and you stipulated for me half the profit, then the statement is given to the owner regarding the profit share, and to the mudarib regarding the amount; because profit is earned by condition, and it is derived from the owner's side.
And whichever of them brings evidence, his evidence is accepted as it is. If both bring evidence in this case, the owner's evidence is preferable regarding the amount of capital, and the mudarib's evidence is preferable regarding the amount of profit, because it is more substantiating.
[4] His saying: And if someone says...etc.; meaning if someone who has one thousand says: He has made profit on it, it is a mudarabah...
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage deals with disputes between the mudarib and the capital owner. The main ruling: if the mudarib claims he received 1000 as capital and made 1000 profit, while the owner claims he gave 2000, the mudarib's statement is accepted with oath. Zufar and the first opinion of Abu Hanifa hold that the owner is believed because he denies the profit claim. However, the relied upon position (mufta bihi) is that the mudarib is believed because the dispute is over the amount received; the receiver is considered more knowledgeable. This applies whether the receiver is a guarantor (like a ghāṣib) or a trustee (like a depositary). If the dispute is about the legal nature (loan, deposit, trade goods), the owner is believed. If the dispute involves both capital amount and profit share conditions, the owner is believed regarding the profit share (since he sets the condition), and the mudarib regarding the capital amount. If both bring evidence, the owner's evidence prevails on capital, the mudarib's on profit because it's more specific.

Key Terms
قابض (qabid): The receiver of the capital or goods; in this context, the mudarib who received the capital.
يمين (yamin): An oath taken by the person whose statement is accepted to confirm his claim.
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence, usually testimonial proof. If both parties bring evidence, preference is given to the one whose evidence is more specific.
زفر (Zufar): Imam Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl, a prominent Hanafi jurist and student of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the mudarib says he was given 1000 as capital and made 1000 profit, and the owner says he gave 2000, who is believed according to the mufta bihi Hanafi position?
A) The owner, because he denies the profit.
B) The mudarib, because the dispute is over the amount received.
C) Neither, they must provide witnesses.
D) The mudarib only if he has a written contract.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi position is that the mudarib is believed about the amount of capital received, with oath, because he is the receiver and more knowledgeable.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate

Mudarib's Word Accepted in Dispute over Capital and Profit
Ruling with proof on mudarib's acceptance in quantity disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whose word is accepted in a mudarabah dispute over the amount of capital and profit, and explain the proof and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
In disputes over quantity received, the receiver's word is accepted; for contract nature, the owner's word is accepted.

When a mudarib and rabb al-mal disagree about how much capital was given and how much profit was earned, whose statement is legally preferred? The Hanafi school answers based on whether the dispute is about quantity or about the nature of the contract. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and the internal disagreement within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute scenario
Consider the case where the mudarib has 2000 in hand. He claims: 'You paid me 1000 capital, and I earned 1000 profit.' The rabb al-mal says: 'I paid 2000 capital, and there is no profit.' Recognize that the disagreement is about the amount of capital and profit.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, the mudarib is believed with his oath. His word is taken over the amount of capital and profit because the dispute is about the quantity received.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Zufar and the early opinion of Abu Hanifa held that the rabb al-mal's word is taken because he denies the profit claim. The later preferred view is the opposite, as adopted by the majority of Hanafi scholars.
4
Examine the proof (dalil)
The proof is: the dispute is about the amount received (مقدار المقبوض). The receiver (qabid) is the mudarib, who knows better what he received. Hence his word is preferred. This is a qiyas based on the general principle that the receiver's word is trusted in quantity disputes.
5
Distinguish exceptions
If the dispute is about the nature of the contract (loan, deposit, bida'a), the rabb al-mal is believed. Also, when both parties produce evidence, each is accepted for what it supports: owner's evidence for capital, mudarib's for profit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الاختلاف
وصدق مضارب قال : ألف دفعته إليّ، وألف ربحت ، لا مالك قال : الكل دَفَعْت ، وعند زُفَرَ الله وهو القول الأول لأبي حنيفة له القول لرب المال ؛ لأنَّهُ يُنْكِرُ دعوى المضارب الربح ، ولنا : أن الاختلاف في مقدار المقبوض ، فالقول للقابض مع اليمين.
[ ١ ] قوله : وصدق...الخ ؛ يعني إذا كان مع المضارب ألفان، فقال المضارب لرب المال : دفعت إلي ألفاً وربحت ألفاً، وقال المالك : لا ؛ بل دفعت إليك الألفين، فالقولُ قول المضارب.
(۲) قوله : لأنه...الخ ؛ يعني لأن المضارب يدعي عليه الشركة في الربح ، ورب المال ينكره ، والقولُ يكون للمنكر. [٣] قوله : ولنا...الخ ؛ يعني إنَّ الاختلاف بينهما حقيقة في مقدار المقبوض ، وفي مثل هذا الاختلاف يكون القولُ قول القابض، سواءً كان ضميناً كالغاصب، أو أميناً كالمودع ؛ لكون القابض أعرف.
بخلاف ما إذا وقع الاختلاف في صفة المقبوض من كونه قرضاً أو وديعة أو بضاعة، فالقول فيه قول رب المال، ولو قال رب المال : رأس المال ألفان، وشرطتُ لكَ ثلث الربح ، قال المضارب : رأس المال ألف، وشرطت لي نصف الربح، فالقول يكون لرب المال في الربح، وللمضارب في القدر ؛ لأن الربح يستحق بالشرط، وهو مستفاد من جهة ربِّ المال.
وأيهما أقام البينة تقبل بيّنته كاسمها ، وإن أقاما البينة في هذه الصورة كانت بينة رب المال أولى في مقدار رأس المال، وبينة المضارب أولى في مقدار الربح؛ لأنها أكثر إثباتا.
Chapter on Disputes. And the mudarib is believed when he says: 'I paid you one thousand and I earned one thousand profit,' not the owner when he says: 'I paid all two thousand.' According to Zufar and the first opinion of Abu Hanifa, the owner's word is taken because he denies the mudarib's claim of profit. And for us: the dispute is about the amount received, so the word is of the receiver with an oath. [1] His saying: 'And he is believed... etc.' means when the mudarib has two thousand, and says to the owner: 'You paid me one thousand and I earned one thousand profit,' and the owner says: 'No, I paid you two thousand,' then the mudarib's word is taken. [3] His saying: 'And for us... etc.' means the dispute between them is in reality about the amount received, and in such a dispute the word is of the receiver, whether he is a guarantor like a usurper or a trustee like a depositary, because the receiver knows better. Contrary to when the dispute is about the quality of the received property — whether it is a loan, deposit, or bida'a — the word is of the owner. And whichever of them presents evidence, his evidence is accepted as usual. And if both present evidence in this scenario, the owner's evidence is given precedence regarding the amount of capital, and the mudarib's evidence regarding the amount of profit, because it establishes more.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof discussing disputes between the mudarib (agent) and rabb al-mal (capital owner) over the amount of capital and profit. The author first states the ruling: the mudarib is believed when he claims that the capital was one thousand and he earned profit, against the owner's claim that the capital was two thousand. The proof is that the dispute is about the quantity received, and the receiver (mudarib) knows best. The author notes that there is an intra-Hanafi disagreement: Zufar and the early opinion of Abu Hanifa gave the word to the owner. But the relied-upon position is that the mudarib is believed because the dispute concerns the amount received. The author then distinguishes cases where the dispute is about the nature of the contract (loan, deposit, etc.) — in those cases the owner is believed. Also, when both parties produce evidence, each is accepted on what it supports: the owner's evidence on capital, the mudarib's on profit.

Key Terms
مضارب (mudarib): The agent in a mudarabah contract who invests the capital and claims profit.
رب المال (rabb al-mal): The capital owner who provides funds for mudarabah.
قابض (qabid): The person who receives and holds the property; here, the mudarib.
بضاعة (bida'a): Goods given for trade without profit-sharing; a type of contract distinct from mudarabah.

Key Takeaway
In mudarabah disputes over the amount of capital or profit, the mudarib's word is accepted with oath; over the nature of the contract, the rabb al-mal's word is accepted.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing

Whose Word is Accepted in Mudarabah Disputes?
Ruling on disputes when a person claims mudarabah and profit, but the worker denies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who is believed in a mudarabah dispute when the worker denies the mudarabah claim, and explain the rationale based on the denial of profit transfer.

Core Idea
In mudarabah disputes, the denier is believed with oath because he denies the claimant's assertion of obligation.

When a person claims that funds were given as mudarabah and profit was made, but the alleged worker (Zaid) denies this and claims it was a bida'a (a non-profit-sharing trade), whose word is accepted? The Hanafi school provides a clear procedural rule based on the principle that the denier's word is taken with oath, as the claimant is asserting an obligation. This lesson unpacks this ruling and its parallels, including cases where the owner specifies a type of trade and how evidence is prioritized.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
There are two parties: the person with money claims it was a mudarabah with Zaid and that profit was made. Zaid denies the mudarabah and claims it was a bida'a (goods for trade without profit-sharing).
The dispute is about the nature of the contract and the obligation to share profit.
2
State the ruling
Zaid (the alleged worker) is believed with his oath. The text says: 'صُدِّق زيد إن قال : بضاعة' (Zaid is believed if he says it is a bida'a).
The ruling applies because Zaid denies the claim of profit or any transfer of ownership.
3
Understand the rationale
The claimant is asserting an obligation (profit sharing or ownership transfer). The denier's word is taken because the original principle is the absence of such obligation (al-asl bara'at al-dhimmah).
The same principle applies analogously if the possessor claims a loan and Zaid claims a deposit or bida'a.
4
Apply the analogy
The commentary extends the ruling: if the possessor says 'loan' and Zaid says 'bida'a' or 'deposit', Zaid is believed. Similarly, if the roles reverse (owner claims loan, mudarib claims mudarabah), the mudarib is believed because the owner is now the claimant of guarantee.
The key is who is denying the claim of an obligation.
5
Analyze specification and evidence
If the owner says he specified a type of trade, the mudarib is believed because the default in mudarabah is generality. For evidence, if both present evidence, the later evidence prevails if times are known; otherwise the owner's evidence is preferred because it establishes guarantee.
These rules ensure consistency in dispute resolution.

[3] His saying: 'The mudarib is believed' applies, and the evidence of whoever presents it is accepted. This is in Al-Bahr and others.

Commentary
This passage addresses disputes when a third party (a person in possession of money) claims that Zaid took it as mudarabah and made profit, but Zaid denies and claims it was a bida'a (goods for trade without profit-sharing). The ruling states that Zaid is believed with his oath because he denies the claim of profit or any obligation to share profit. This is analogous to cases where the possessor claims a loan and Zaid claims bida'a or deposit: the owner (Zaid) is believed. The commentary then discusses cases where the owner (rabb al-mal) says he specified a type of trade; then the mudarib is believed because the default in mudarabah is generality. If both parties present evidence, the later evidence prevails if times are marked; otherwise the owner's evidence is given preference. This is from Al-Bahr al-Raiq.

Key Terms
بضاعة (bida'a): Goods given for trade without profit-sharing; in this context, Zaid claims it is a bida'a, denying mudarabah.
وديعة (wadi'a): A deposit; the possessor claims it is a deposit, but Zaid denies.
تمليك (tamlik): Transfer of ownership; Zaid denies the claim of transfer of profit ownership.
ينكر (yunkir): He denies; the denier's word is taken with oath.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate
