When Owner and Mudarib Disagree on Investment Type: Hanafi Ruling
Ruling on conflicting claims and evidence in mudarabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the owner's statement is taken in mudarabah disputes and identify when evidence shifts the burden.

Core Idea
In mudarabah, the owner's word prevails because permission originates from him; the mudarib must bring evidence to claim otherwise.

In a mudarabah partnership, what happens if the owner and the mudarib disagree about what commodity they agreed to trade? The Hanafi school gives clear guidance: the owner's statement is taken, backed by his oath, because he is the source of permission. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the exceptions when evidence is brought.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
The owner claims one type of commodity (e.g., wheat) and the mudarib claims another (e.g., barley). Both agree there was a mudarabah, but disagree on the specific authorization.
This is a dispute over the scope of permission, not over the existence of the contract.
2
Apply the default rule
Without evidence, the owner's statement is taken with his oath. The reason is that permission (idhn) originates from the owner, so he knows best what he permitted.
The owner's oath is required; the mudarib's claim alone is insufficient.
3
Contrast with agency (wakalah)
In agency, the default is particularity; the agent must prove general authority. In mudarabah, the default is also particularity but the owner's word is accepted because he is the source of idhn.
This highlights that the owner's authority is central.
4
Analyze the evidence scenario
If both parties produce witnesses (bayyinah), the mudarib's evidence is considered first because he needs to prove he had permission for the type he claims to avoid liability. The owner does not need evidence as his claim is supported by the default.
The burden of proof shifts to the mudarib when he contradicts the default.
5
Handle timed evidence
If evidence includes dates, the later-dated evidence prevails (because the later contract abrogates the earlier). If no dates or equal dates, the owner's evidence is given precedence because it establishes something not previously established.
Timing resolves the conflict; otherwise, owner's evidence wins.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المضاربة المضارب الذي يضارب
ولو ادعى كل نوعاً صُدِّقَ المالك
بخلاف الوكالة ؛ لأنَّ الأصل فيها الخصوص" (ولو ادعى كل نوعاً صُدِّقَ المالك) : أي مع اليمين ؛ لأنَّ الإذنَ يستفاد من جهته .
[١) قوله : لأن الأصل فيه الخصوص ؛ ولا يثبتُ فيه العموم إلا بالتنصيص. [٢] قوله : ولو ادعى كل...الخ ؛ يعني لو ادعى كلُّ واحدٍ من المالك والمضارب نوعاً مغايراً لما يدعيه الآخر، بان قال رب المال في البرّ، وقال المضارب في الطعام، فالقولُ يكون للمالك مع يمينه ؛ لأنهما اتفقا على التخصيص، والإذن يستفاد من جهته، فيكون القول له. ولو أقاما البينة فيكون البينة بينةُ المضارب ؛ لاحتياجه إلى إثبات الإذن في نوع يدعي الإذن فيه، حتى ينتفي الضمان عنه، وعدم حاجة الآخر، أعني رب المال إلى البينة ؛ لأن ما يدعيه ثبت بقوله ، إذ هو التمسك بالأصل.
ولو وقتت البينتان وقتاً ؛ بأن قال رب المال : دفعتُ إليك مضاربة أن تعمل في بز في رمضان وقال المضارب دفعت إلي لأن اعمل في طعام في شوال، أو بالعكس، فأقاما البينة، فبينة صاحب الوقتِ الأخير أولى ؛ لأن آخر الشرطين ينتقض الأول. وإن لم يوقت البينتان، أو وقتا على السواء، أو وقتت إحداهما دون الأخرى يقضي بينة رب المال ؛ لأنه تعذر القضاء بهما معاً ؛ لأنهما لا يقعان معاً، ولا على الترتيب ؛ لأنَّ الشهود لم يشهدوا بالترتيب، وإذا تعذر القضاء بالأمرين تعذر العمل بالبينتين، فيعمل ببينة ربِّ المال ؛ لأنها تثبت ما ليس بثابت).
(1) ينظر: «التبيين»(٥ : ٧٦).
وجي
Book of Mudarabah. The mudarib who enters into mudarabah. If each claims a different type, the owner is believed – unlike in agency, because the basis in agency is particularity. (And if each claims a different type, the owner is believed): i.e., with his oath, because permission is derived from him. [1) He said: because the basis in it is particularity, and generality is not established except by explicit text. [2] He said: and if each claims...etc.; meaning if each of the owner and mudarib claims a type different from what the other claims, such as the owner saying in wheat and the mudarib saying in food, then the statement is the owner's with his oath; because they both agree on specification, and permission is derived from him, so his statement is taken. If they both produce evidence, then the evidence is the mudarib's evidence; because he needs to prove permission for the type he claims to be permitted in, so that liability is negated from him, while the other (the owner) does not need evidence because what he claims is established by his statement, as he is adhering to the original. If the two pieces of evidence are timed; such as the owner saying: I gave you mudarabah to work in cloth in Ramadan, and the mudarib saying: you gave me (mudarabah) to work in food in Shawwal, or the opposite, and they both produce evidence, then the evidence of the one with the later time is preferred; because the later of two conditions abrogates the earlier. If the two pieces of evidence are not timed, or are timed equally, or one is timed and the other not, then the owner's evidence is given precedence; because it is impossible to give effect to both, as they cannot occur together, nor in sequence since the witnesses did not testify to order, and when it is impossible to give effect to both matters, it is impossible to act on both pieces of evidence, so the owner's evidence is acted upon because it establishes something not previously established. (1) See: al-Tabyin (5:76). Waji [possibly incomplete].
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah deals with a dispute in a mudarabah partnership regarding the type of commodity to be traded. The core ruling is that if the owner (rabb al-mal) and the mudarib each claim a different type (e.g., the owner says wheat, the mudarib says barley), the owner's statement is taken as true, supported by his oath. The reasoning is that permission (idhn) for the mudarabah originates from the owner; therefore, the owner's word is authoritative regarding what he permitted. The text contrasts this with agency (wakalah), where the default is particularity, meaning the agent must prove a general authorization if claimed. In mudarabah, the same principle applies: the owner specifies the type, and his word is believed. If both parties bring witnesses (bayyinah), the mudarib must present evidence because he needs to prove he had permission for the type he claims, in order to avoid liability (daman). The owner, on the other hand, relies on the default (asl) that his statement is sufficient. If both pieces of evidence are timed (e.g., one date for a wheat contract and a later date for a food contract), the evidence with the later date prevails because the later contract abrogates the earlier one. If no timing exists, both are timed equally, or only one is timed, then the owner's evidence is given precedence because it's impossible to reconcile both conflicting testimonies, and the owner's evidence establishes what was not previously established (i.e., his version). This ruling is consistent with the Hanafi position that the owner is the source of permission and his word is trusted in case of dispute.

Key Terms
المضاربة (al-mudarabah): A partnership where the owner provides capital and the mudarib provides labor, with profits shared according to agreement.
المالك (al-malik): The owner of capital in a mudarabah contract; also called rabb al-mal. His permission defines the scope of the mudarib's authority.
البينة (al-bayyinah): Legal evidence, typically testimony of two male witnesses or one male and two females in financial matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a mudarabah dispute, if the owner claims the contract was for trading wheat and the mudarib claims it was for barley, and neither has witnesses, whose statement is accepted?
A) The mudarib's, because he is the trustee.
B) The owner's, because permission comes from him.
C) The mudarib's, because he performs the work.
D) The owner's, because he provided the capital.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the owner's word is accepted in mudarabah disputes over the type of investment because he is the source of permission; the mudarib must provide evidence to prove otherwise.
